Salah — Prayer
intermediate
8 min
Eating and Drinking During Salah: Invalidating Acts and Thresholds
Commentary on the ruling of eating and drinking during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on eating/drinking during prayer and apply the chickpea threshold to determine invalidation.

Core Idea
Eating or drinking any amount invalidates prayer, except for residual food less than a chickpea, which is merely disliked.

This lesson delves into the detailed rulings on eating and drinking during prayer. The passage draws a parallel with fasting and establishes a threshold based on the size of a chickpea. It also addresses the case of blood between teeth and an intra-Hanafi difference regarding a sesame seed. Understanding these details is essential for safeguarding the validity of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the general ruling
Eating or drinking invalidates prayer, whether done deliberately or forgetfully.
The text says: 'فإن فعل ذلك: بطلت صلاته، سواء أكل عامداً أو ناسياً'.
2
Note the parallel with fasting
What invalidates fasting also invalidates prayer, and what does not, does not.
This is quoted from al-Ghayah, providing a consistent standard.
3
Analyze the chickpea threshold
If food stuck between teeth is less than a chickpea and swallowed, prayer is valid but disliked. If it is a chickpea or more, prayer and fasting are invalidated.
The measure 'الحمصة' (chickpea) is the benchmark.
4
Examine the case of blood
If blood between teeth is swallowed and saliva predominates, prayer is not invalidated.
5
Consider the sesame seed ikhtilaf
According to the well-known view (mashhur), swallowing a sesame seed invalidates prayer. There is a riwaya from Abu Hanifa that it does not. The relied-upon position is the mashhur.
This intra-Hanafi dispute is resolved by adopting the stronger view.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
مكروهات الصلاة
ولا يردُّ السلام بلسانه ولا بيده.
ولا يتربَّعُ إلا من عذر.
ولا يأكل، ولا يشرب.
ويكره أن يُغمض عينيه في الصلاة.
وأن يغطي فاه؛ لأنه يُشبه فعل المجوس، إلا إذا تثاءب: فله ذلك؛ لما ذكرناه آنفاً.
قوله: (ولا يرد السلام بلسانه، ولا بيده). فإن رده بلسانه: بطلت صلاته. وكذا إذا صافح بنية السلام: تفسد أيضاً. وإن أشار برد السلام برأسه، أو بيده أو بأصبعه: لا تفسد، إلا أنه يكره. ويكره السلام على القارئ، والمصلي، والجالس على البول والغائط.
قوله: (ولا يتربَّع إلا من عذر؛ لأن فيه ترك سُنَّة القعود. فإن كان به عذر: جاز؛ لأن الأعذار تؤثر في فروض الصلاة، فكذا في سننها).
قوله: (ولا يأكل، ولا يشرب). فإن فعل ذلك: بطلت صلاته، سواء أكل عامداً أو ناسياً؛ لأنه معنى ينافي الصلاة، وحالة الصلاة مذكرة.
قال في «الغاية»: ما أفسد الصوم: أفسد الصلاة، وما لا: فلا. حتى إذا كان بين أسنانه شيء من طعام، فابتلعه: إن كان دون الحمصة: لم تفسد صلاته؛ لأنه تبع لريقه، إلا أنه يكره. وإن كان قدر الحمصة، فصاعداً: أفسد الصلاة والصوم. ولو ابتلع دماً بين أسنانه: لم تفسد صلاته إذا كانت الغلبة للريق. وإن ابتلع سمسمةً: أفسدت على المشهور، وعن أبي حنيفة: لا.
Disliked acts of prayer. He does not return the greeting with his tongue nor with his hand. And he does not sit cross-legged except due to an excuse. And he does not eat nor drink. And it is disliked to close his eyes in prayer. And to cover his mouth because it resembles the act of the Magians, except if he yawns: then it is permissible for him; due to what we mentioned earlier. His statement: 'And he does not return the greeting with his tongue nor with his hand.' If he returns it with his tongue, his prayer is invalidated. Likewise, if he shakes hands with the intention of greeting, it also invalidates. And if he gestures returning the greeting with his head, or his hand, or his finger: it does not invalidate, but it is disliked. And it is disliked to greet the one reciting Quran, the one praying, and the one sitting to relieve himself. His statement: 'And he does not sit cross-legged except due to an excuse; because in it is leaving the sunnah of sitting. If he has an excuse: it is permissible; because excuses affect the obligations of prayer, likewise in its sunan.' His statement: 'And he does not eat nor drink.' If he does that, his prayer is invalidated, whether he eats deliberately or forgetfully; because it is a meaning that contradicts prayer, and the state of prayer is one of remembrance. He said in al-Ghayah: Whatever invalidates fasting invalidates prayer, and whatever does not, then not. Even if there is something of food between his teeth, and he swallows it: if it is less than a chickpea: his prayer is not invalidated; because it is a follow-up to his saliva, except that it is disliked. And if it is the size of a chickpea or more: it invalidates prayer and fasting. And if he swallows blood between his teeth: his prayer is not invalidated if the saliva predominates. And if he swallows a sesame seed: it invalidates according to the well-known view, and from Abu Hanifa: no.
Source pages p. 403

Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayrah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer. The commentator expands on the base text of Al-Quduri. He begins by listing several disliked actions: not returning the salam verbally or by hand gesture, sitting cross-legged without excuse, eating and drinking, closing eyes, and covering the mouth. Each has a specific ruling: The text distinguishes between actions that invalidate prayer and those that are merely disliked but do not invalidate. For example, responding to salam verbally invalidates, while gesturing with head or hand does not, though it is still disliked. Similarly, eating or drinking invalidates prayer whether done deliberately or forgetfully. The commentator then cites al-Ghayah to draw a parallel with fasting: what invalidates fasting also invalidates prayer. This leads to a detailed discussion of swallowing food stuck in teeth: if it is smaller than a chickpea and swallowed passively with saliva, prayer is valid but disliked; if larger, it invalidates. Swallowing blood between teeth is valid if saliva dominates. There is also a minority view from Abu Hanifa that swallowing a sesame seed does not invalidate, but the relied-upon position (mashhur) is that it does. The commentator emphasizes that excuses can permit normally disliked postures, as even obligations are affected by excuses, so sunan are more easily excused. The overall message is that while these acts are discouraged, their legal consequences vary from mere dislike to complete invalidation.

Key Terms
الحمصة (al-himmisah): A chickpea, used as a standard measure for the size of swallowed food that invalidates prayer.
سمسمة (simsimah): A sesame seed, mentioned in the intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the size of food that, if swallowed from between the teeth, invalidates the prayer?
A) Any amount
B) Less than a chickpea
C) A chickpea or more
D) A sesame seed

Key Takeaway
Eating or drinking invalidates prayer, with a dispensation for residual food less than a chickpea; the mashhur view holds that even a sesame seed invalidates.

Other Disliked Acts in Salah: Sitting Cross-Legged, Closing Eyes, Covering Mouth
Commentary on three specific disliked acts in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to list the disliked acts of sitting cross-legged, closing eyes, and covering the mouth during prayer, and explain when they are permissible.

Core Idea
Sitting cross-legged without excuse is makruh; closing eyes and covering mouth are also makruh, except covering mouth is allowed when yawning.

This lesson covers three specific disliked acts in prayer: sitting cross-legged during the sitting position, closing the eyes, and covering the mouth. The passage provides rulings and exceptions for each. Understanding these helps avoid unnecessary acts that reduce the reward of salah.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three actions
Sitting cross-legged, closing eyes, covering mouth are all mentioned as disliked.
They are part of the general list of makruhat.
2
Determine the general ruling for sitting cross-legged
It is disliked unless there is an excuse. The excuse can be any legitimate reason (e.g., leg injury).
The text says 'إلا من عذر'.
3
Understand the reason for dislike
Sitting cross-legged abandons the sunnah posture of sitting (iftaarash or tawarruk).
The text: 'لأن فيه ترك سُنَّة القعود'.
4
Determine the ruling for closing eyes
It is disliked without exception mentioned.
The text simply says 'يكره أن يُغمض عينيه في الصلاة'.
5
Determine the ruling for covering mouth
It is disliked because it resembles the Magians, except when yawning, then it is permissible because the sunnah recommends covering the mouth during a yawn.
The text: 'إلا إذا تثاءب: فله ذلك'.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

ولا يأكل، ولا يشرب.

And to cover his mouth because it resembles the act of the Magians, except if he yawns: then it is permissible for him; due to what we mentioned earlier. Commentary
This passage from Al-Jawharah al-Nayrah discusses various disliked acts (makruhat) in prayer. The commentator expands on the base text of Al-Quduri. He begins by listing several disliked actions: not returning the salam verbally or by hand gesture, sitting cross-legged without excuse, eating and drinking, closing eyes, and covering the mouth. The overall message is that while these acts are discouraged, their legal consequences vary from mere dislike to complete invalidation.

Key Terms
مكروه (makruh): An action that is disliked in prayer; doing it does not invalidate the prayer (except where specified) but reduces reward.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the ruling on sitting cross-legged during prayer if the person has a leg injury?
A) Still disliked
B) Permissible due to excuse
C) Invalidates prayer
D) Recommended

Key Takeaway
Sitting cross-legged without excuse, closing eyes, and covering mouth are disliked; however, excuses and yawning permit the respective acts.

Swallowing Food and Blood During Prayer: The Hanafi Threshold
Rulings on what invalidates prayer when swallowing objects.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the size threshold for food and the condition for blood that determine whether swallowing invalidates prayer, and apply these rules to common scenarios.

Core Idea
A swallowed object invalidates prayer only if it reaches the size of a chickpea or if blood predominates over saliva.

In this lesson, we examine what happens when a person swallows food residue or blood while praying. The Hanafi school sets a clear threshold: a small amount is excused, but a substantial amount nullifies the prayer. We also learn the general principle that any invalidator of fasting also invalidates prayer.

Guided Path
1
Understand the general rule
Memorize the principle quoted from al-Ghaya: whatever invalidates fasting invalidates prayer. This means the threshold for fasting (like the chickpea) transfers to prayer.
2
Identify the amount of food
Distinguish between less than a chickpea (does not invalidate, but makruh) and a chickpea or more (invalidates both prayer and fasting).
The chickpea is a fixed measure (al-ḥimṣa).
3
Analyze the case of blood
If blood on the teeth is swallowed, it does not invalidate if saliva is dominant. If blood is dominant, it invalidates.
This ruling is based on istihsan because the blood is negligible.
4
Note the dislike
Even if not invalidating, swallowing any food residue is makruh—so it should be avoided.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «الغاية»: ما أفسد الصوم: أفسد الصلاة، وما لا: فلا. حتى إذا كان بين أسنانه شيء من طعام، فابتلعه: إن كان دون الحمصة : لم تفسد صلاته ؛ لأنه تبع لريقه، إلا أنه يكره. وإن كان قدر الحمصة، فصاعداً: أفسد الصلاة والصوم. ولو ابتلع دماً بين أسنانه : لم تفسد صلاته إذا كانت الغلبة للريق. - وإن ابتلع سمسمةً : أفسدت على المشهور، وعن أبي حنيفة: لا
He said in al-Ghaya: Whatever invalidates fasting invalidates prayer, and what does not, does not. So if there is something of food between his teeth and he swallows it: if it is less than a chickpea, his prayer is not invalidated because it is a follower of his saliva, except that it is disliked. And if it is the size of a chickpea or more, it invalidates prayer and fasting. And if he swallows blood between his teeth, his prayer is not invalidated if saliva predominates. And if he swallows a sesame seed, it invalidates according to the mashhur, and from Abu Hanifa: no.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer, specifically regarding swallowing. The author quotes al-Ghaya's principle: anything that nullifies fasting also nullifies prayer, except that the inverse is not necessarily true. The primary examples are: (1) Swallowing food residue less than a chickpea does not invalidate prayer because it follows saliva, though it is makruh. (2) If the residue equals or exceeds a chickpea, it invalidates both prayer and fasting. (3) Swallowing blood from teeth does not invalidate prayer if saliva is dominant; this is based on istihsan because the blood is negligible. (4) There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a sesame seed: the mashhur (relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds that it invalidates, but a narration from Abu Hanifa states it does not. The mufta bihi is the mashhur position, as it accords with the general principle that any solid substance reaching the stomach invalidates.

Key Terms
الحمصة (al-ḥimṣa): A chickpea, used as a measure for the amount of food that invalidates prayer.
السمسمة (al-simsima): A sesame seed, the smallest solid object considered possibly invalidating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on swallowing food between the teeth that is less than a chickpea during prayer?
A) Invalidates prayer
B) Does not invalidate but is disliked
C) Permissible and not disliked
D) Invalidates only if intentional

Key Takeaway
The size threshold of a chickpea and the dominance of saliva are key factors in determining whether swallowing invalidates prayer.

The Sesame Seed: An Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Prayer Invalidity
Intra-Hanafi dispute on whether swallowing a sesame seed invalidates prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to identify the two Hanafi positions on swallowing a sesame seed during prayer and explain why the mashhur view is preferred using the tarjih mechanism.

Core Idea
A sesame seed is the minimum measure for invalidity according to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad; Abu Hanifa dissents.

This lesson focuses on a specific point of intra-Hanafi disagreement: does swallowing a single sesame seed during prayer invalidate it? The mashhur position of the Sahibayn (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) says yes, while Abu Hanifa says no. We examine the difference and the relied-upon ruling.

Guided Path
1
Recall the general principle
From al-Ghaya: whatever invalidates fasting invalidates prayer. For fasting, any solid food reaching the stomach invalidates, regardless of amount. So applying that to prayer, even a small seed could invalidate.
2
State Abu Hanifa's view
Abu Hanifa held that a sesame seed does not invalidate prayer. His reasoning likely based on the idea that it is too small to constitute 'eating' in the legal sense.
This is a weak (marjuh) narration according to later Hanafis.
3
State the mashhur view
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad held that swallowing a sesame seed invalidates prayer. They argued that any solid matter entering the stomach invalidates, consistent with the fasting analogy.
This is the mufta bihi.
4
Analyze the tarjih
The mashhur view is preferred because it is more precautionary (ihtiyat) and aligns with the general rule that any solid invalidates. The narration from Abu Hanifa is considered weaker (shadh).

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قال في «الغاية»: ما أفسد الصوم: أفسد الصلاة، وما لا: فلا. حتى إذا كان بين أسنانه شيء من طعام، فابتلعه: إن كان دون الحمصة : لم تفسد صلاته ؛ لأنه تبع لريقه، إلا أنه يكره. وإن كان قدر الحمصة، فصاعداً: أفسد الصلاة والصوم. ولو ابتلع دماً بين أسنانه : لم تفسد صلاته إذا كانت الغلبة للريق. - وإن ابتلع سمسمةً : أفسدت على المشهور، وعن أبي حنيفة: لا
He said in al-Ghaya: Whatever invalidates fasting invalidates prayer, and what does not, does not. So if there is something of food between his teeth and he swallows it: if it is less than a chickpea, his prayer is not invalidated because it is a follower of his saliva, except that it is disliked. And if it is the size of a chickpea or more, it invalidates prayer and fasting. And if he swallows blood between his teeth, his prayer is not invalidated if saliva predominates. And if he swallows a sesame seed, it invalidates according to the mashhur, and from Abu Hanifa: no.
Source pages p. 404

Commentary
This passage is a ruling on invalidators (mufsidat) of prayer, specifically regarding swallowing. The author quotes al-Ghaya's principle: anything that nullifies fasting also nullifies prayer, except that the inverse is not necessarily true. The primary examples are: (1) Swallowing food residue less than a chickpea does not invalidate prayer because it follows saliva, though it is makruh. (2) If the residue equals or exceeds a chickpea, it invalidates both prayer and fasting. (3) Swallowing blood from teeth does not invalidate prayer if saliva is dominant; this is based on istihsan because the blood is negligible. (4) There is an intra-Hanafi ikhtilaf regarding a sesame seed: the mashhur (relied-upon view of Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) holds that it invalidates, but a narration from Abu Hanifa states it does not. The mufta bihi is the mashhur position, as it accords with the general principle that any solid substance reaching the stomach invalidates.

Key Terms
الحمصة (al-ḥimṣa): A chickpea, used as a measure for the amount of food that invalidates prayer.
السمسمة (al-simsima): A sesame seed, the smallest solid object considered possibly invalidating.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What is the relied-upon (mufta bihi) ruling regarding swallowing a sesame seed during prayer?
A) It does not invalidate, according to Abu Hanifa
B) It invalidates, according to the Sahibayn
C) It is disliked but not invalidating
D) It is permissible with no dislike

Key Takeaway
The mashhur position in the Hanafi school is that swallowing a sesame seed invalidates prayer.

Rulings on Preceding Hadath: Leaving and Building
Definition and conditions for building on prayer after hadath.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the conditions for building upon prayer after an involuntary hadath and identify when building is prohibited.

Core Idea
Building on prayer after involuntary hadath is allowed if you leave immediately and are not the imam.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayira explains the ruling when a person is overtaken by a state that invalidates wudu during prayer. It distinguishes between involuntary and voluntary causes and sets conditions for continuing the same prayer after renewing wudu. Understanding these rulings helps maintain the validity of prayer while providing ease for unforeseen events.

Guided Path
1
Understand the terms sabq and ghalaba
Sabq means the hadath occurred without your knowledge or intent. Ghalaba means you were aware but unable to control it. Both are involuntary, and building is allowed for both.
The text only mentions sabq explicitly but the commentary extends the ruling to ghalaba.
2
Identify the ruling and its conditions
If hadath overtakes you, you must leave immediately, perform wudu, and build upon your prayer. However, you cannot be an imam; imams must appoint a successor.
The Arabic 'انصرف وتوضأ وبنى على صلاته إن لم يكن إماماً' encapsulates the core ruling.
3
Note the exception for forceful voluntary acts
If the hadath is caused by sneezing, clearing throat, or coughing that forcefully expels wind, building is not allowed. This is the correct opinion (huwa al-sahih).
The text links the exception to 'خروج بقوته ريح' – wind exiting with force.
4
Define immediate leaving
Leaving must be immediate – without any delay. If you delay for the time it takes to perform one rak'ah (e.g., reciting a long surah), the prayer becomes invalid.
The commentary specifies 'من ساعته من غير توقف' – from that very moment without stopping.
5
Review permissible actions while leaving
While leaving, you are allowed to walk, scoop water from a vessel, turn away from the qibla, wash impurity, and perform istinja' as long as your awrah is not exposed (e.g., from under the shirt).
These actions are necessary to complete wudu and remove impurities.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام سبق الحدث فإن سبقه الحدث ،انصرف وتوضأ وبنى على صلاته إن لم يكن إماماً . سبق: بغير علمه وقصده. والغلبة : بعلمه، لكن لم يقدر على ضبطه. ولو عطس، فسبقه الحدث، أو تنحنح، أو سعل، فخرج بقوته ريح: فإنه لا يبني، هو الصحيح. قوله : انصرف : أي من ساعته من غير توقف، فإن لبث ساعةً قدر ما يؤدي ركناً: بطلت صلاته. وإذا انصرف يباح له المشي، والاغترافُ من الإناء، والانحراف عن القبلة، وغسل النجاسة، والاستنجاء إذا أمكنه من غير كشف عورته، بأن يكون من تحت القميص.
Rulings on Preceding Hadath. If the hadath overtakes him, he leaves and performs wudu and builds upon his prayer if he was not an imam. 'Preceding' is without his knowledge and intent. 'Overcoming' is with his knowledge but unable to control it. If he sneezes and hadath overtakes him, or he clears his throat, or coughs, and wind exits with force, then he does not build, that is the correct opinion. His saying 'he leaves' means immediately without delay, for if he delays for the time it takes to perform a rak'ah, his prayer is invalid. When he leaves, it is permissible for him to walk, scoop from the vessel, turn away from the qibla, wash impurity, and perform istinja' if possible without exposing his private parts, such as from under the shirt.
Source pages p. 405

Commentary
This passage defines and provides rulings on 'sabq al-hadath' (being overtaken by an invalidating event) during prayer. The fiqh term 'sabq' means the hadath occurred without the person's knowledge or intent, while 'ghalaba' means he was aware but unable to control it. In either case, the person must immediately leave the prayer (without delay) to perform wudu. He may then build upon his previous prayer if he was not an imam. However, if the hadath was caused by sneezing, clearing throat, or coughing that forcefully expelled wind, then he cannot build—this is the correct opinion. The commentary explains that 'leaving' must be immediate; if he delays for the time to perform a full rak'ah, the prayer becomes invalid. While leaving, it is permitted to walk, use an utensil, turn away from qibla, wash impurity, and do istinja' as long as awrah is not exposed.

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (sabq al-ḥadath): The occurrence of a hadath (state invalidating wudu) without one's knowledge or intent.
انصرف (inṣarafa): To immediately leave the prayer space upon realizing the hadath.
بنى على صلاته (banā ʿalā ṣalātihi): To continue from where one left off after performing wudu, without starting anew.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if they are overtaken by hadath during prayer without their knowledge?
A) Continue the prayer and ignore it.
B) Leave immediately, perform wudu, and build on the prayer.
C) Leave, perform wudu, and start the prayer anew.
D) Leave the prayer entirely and not return.

Key Takeaway
Building on prayer after involuntary hadath is valid if you leave immediately, perform wudu, and are not leading the prayer; however, if the hadath was caused by a forceful voluntary act, you cannot build.

Salah — Prayer

Rulings of Previous Hadath in Prayer (Sabq al-Hadath)
Explains the rulings of sabaq al-hadath with conditions and scenarios

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi rulings for building prayer after hadath for an imam, follower, and alone person, and determine when it is preferable to restart instead of building.

Core Idea
Building upon prayer after hadath is permissible only if no speech or excessive action occurs, and the need for wudu is genuine.

This passage from the commentary on al-Quduri explains the specifics of 'sabaq al-hadath' — when one's ablution breaks during prayer. The rulings differ depending on whether one is praying alone, as a follower, or as an imam. The text also discusses the conditions that allow building (resuming from where one left off) and the circumstances in which restarting the prayer is preferred.

Guided Path
1
Identify the ruling for the imam
Read the matn: if the imam's wudu breaks, he should appoint a substitute, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer as long as he does not speak.
Appointing a substitute is done by dragging him by his garment to the mihrab.
2
List the conditions that prevent building
Building is not allowed if the person speaks, eats, drinks, draws water from a well (according to al-Karkhi), or carries a vessel with two hands. Intentional hadath (urination/defecation) also prevents building.
Carrying with one hand is permissible; with two hands is considered excess action.
3
Understand the intra-Hanafi dispute on drawing water
Al-Marghinani permits drawing water from a well if no other water is available and building upon the prayer. Al-Karkhi argues that drawing water involves multiple actions that break prayer continuity.
The text does not give a definitive tarjih, but al-Marghinani's view is mentioned favorably.
4
Identify the scenarios for the alone person, follower, and imam
The alone person has a choice to complete his prayer where he made wudu or return to his original spot (returning is preferable). The follower must return to his place unless the imam has finished or there is no barrier; then he can follow from his wudu spot. If the imam returns, he becomes a follower and the substitute becomes imam.
If the original imam invalidates his prayer before the substitute stands in, all prayers are invalid.
5
Determine when restarting is preferred over building
Restarting (istinaf) is better to avoid disagreement, especially for the alone person. For the imam and follower, if they can find another congregation, restarting is better; otherwise, building is better to preserve congregational virtue.
This mufta bihi position is confirmed in al-Fatawa.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام سبق الحدث
فإن كان إماماً : استخلف، وتوضأ، وبنى على صلاته ما لم يتكلم .
ولو وجد ماءً في مكان، وجاوزه إلى مكان آخر: تفسد صلاته؛ لأن هذا مشي من غير حاجة.
قوله: وبنى: من شرط جواز البناء: أن لا يفعل فعلاً ينافي الصلاة، من الأكل والشرب والكلام، والاستقاء من البئر.
وفي المرغيناني له أن يستقي من البئر إذا لم يكن عنده ماء آخر.
وقال الكرخي: لا يبني مع الاستقاء من البئر. ولو بال أو تغوط : لا يبني ؛ لأن هذا حدث عمد، وهو يمنع البناء.
- وإن ملاً الإناء، وحَمَلَه بيدين: لا يبني.
وإن حَمَلَه بيد واحدة: جاز له البناء ؛ لأن الحمل بيدين عمل كثير.
قوله: (فإن كان إماماً : استخلف، وتوضأ، وبنى على صلاته ما لم يتكلم).
كيفية الاستخلاف أن يجره بثوبه إلى المحراب.
ثم المصلي لا يخلو : إما أن يكون منفرداً، أو مقتدياً، أو إماماً:
١- أما إذا كان منفرداً، وسبقه الحدث، فانصرف وتوضأ، فهو بالخيار: إن شاء أتم صلاته في الموضع الذي توضأ فيه، وإن شاء عاد إلى مصلاه، والأفضل العود، وهو اختيار السرخسي (۱) ؛ ليكون مؤدياً جميعها في مكان واحد.
وقيل : الأفضل في الموضع الذي توضأ فيه؛ لما فيه من تقليل المشي.
٢- وأما إذا كان مقتدياً، فانصرف وتوضأ : فإنه يعود إلى مكانه، إلا أن يكون إمامه قد فرغ من صلاته، أو لا يكون بينهما حائل: فيجوز له الاقتداء به وهو في موضعه الذي توضأ فيه.
وإن كان الإمام قد فرغ: جاز له أن يبني على صلاته في الموضع الذي توضأ فيه.
وأما إذا كان إماماً، فانصرف وتوضأ، وعاد إلى مصلاه: صار مأموماً، والإمام هو الثاني ؛ لأنه لما خرج من المسجد : خرج من الإمامة، وصار مؤتماً.
ولو أن الإمام أفسد صلاته قبل أن يقوم الثاني مكانه: فسدت صلاتهم جميعاً.
قوله: (والاستئناف: أفضل)؛ تحرزاً عن شبهة الخلاف.
وهذا في حق الكل عند بعض المشايخ.
وقيل: هذا في حق المنفرد قطعاً، وأما الإمام والمأموم إن كانا يجدان جماعة: فالاستئناف أفضل أيضاً.
وإن كانا لا يجدان : فالبناء أفضلُ ؛ صيانةً لفضيلة الجماعة، وصحح هذا في «الفتاوى».
Rulings of Previous Hadath: If he is an imam: he appoints a substitute, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer as long as he does not speak. And if he finds water in a place and passes over it to another place: his prayer is invalidated because this is walking without need. His statement: 'and builds': from the conditions of permissibility of building is that he does not do an action contrary to prayer, like eating, drinking, speaking, and drawing water from a well. And according to al-Marghinani: he may draw water from the well if he has no other water. And al-Karkhi said: he does not build with drawing water from the well. And if he urinates or defecates: he does not build because this is intentional hadath, and it prevents building. And if he fills the vessel and carries it with two hands: he does not build. And if he carries it with one hand: it is permissible for him to build because carrying with two hands is a lot of action. His statement: (if he is an imam: he appoints a substitute, performs wudu, and builds upon his prayer as long as he does not speak). The manner of appointment is that he drags him by his garment to the mihrab. Then the praying person is not free: either he is alone, or a follower, or an imam: 1- As for if he is alone and hadath precedes him, so he leaves and performs wudu, he has a choice: if he wishes he completes his prayer in the place where he performed wudu, and if he wishes he returns to his prayer place, and the preferable is returning, and this is the choice of al-Sarakhsi, so that he performs all of it in one place. And it is said: the preferable is in the place where he performed wudu because it reduces walking. 2- And as for if he is a follower, so he leaves and performs wudu: then he returns to his place, unless his imam has finished his prayer, or there is no barrier between them: then it is permissible for him to follow the imam while he is in his place where he performed wudu. And if the imam has finished: it is permissible for him to build upon his prayer in the place where he performed wudu. And as for if he is an imam, so he leaves and performs wudu, and returns to his prayer place: he becomes a follower, and the imam is the second one, because when he left the mosque, he left the imamate and became a follower. And if the imam invalidated his prayer before the second one stood in his place: all of their prayers are invalidated. His statement: (and restarting is better) as a precaution against the doubt of disagreement. And this applies to everyone according to some mashayikh. And it is said: this applies to the alone definitively, but as for the imam and the follower, if they can find a congregation: then restarting is also better. And if they cannot find one: then building is better to preserve the virtue of congregation, and this was corrected in al-Fatawa.
Source pages p. 406

Commentary
This passage from the sharh explains the rulings of 'sabaq al-hadath' (when ritual purity is lost unexpectedly during prayer). The author first presents the ruling from the matn: if an imam's ablution breaks, he should appoint a substitute, perform wudu, and then build upon his existing prayer as long as he does not speak. The commentary clarifies that if the imam passes over water without need, the prayer is invalidated because of unnecessary movement. Building is only permissible if no action contrary to prayer is done, such as eating, drinking, speaking, or drawing water from a well. There is an intra-Hanafi dispute on drawing water: according to al-Marghinani, it is allowed if no other water is available, while al-Karkhi forbids building in that case. Intentional urination or defecation prevents building. Carrying a vessel of water with two hands is considered excessive action and prevents building, but carrying with one hand is permissible. The commentary then details the scenarios for the alone person, the follower, and the imam. The alone person has a choice to complete his prayer in the place he made wudu or return to his original spot; the preferable is to return. For the follower, he must return to his place unless his imam has finished or there is no barrier, in which case he may follow the imam from his new location. If the imam himself has finished, the former follower can build in his place. For an imam who leaves and returns, he becomes a follower and the substitute becomes the imam. If the original imam invalidates his prayer before the substitute stands in, all congregational prayers are invalid. Finally, the text discusses whether restarting (istinaf) is better than building. For the alone person, restarting is better to avoid disagreement. For the imam and follower, if they can find a congregation, restarting is better; otherwise, building is better to preserve congregational virtue. This 'mufta bihi' position is confirmed in al-Fatawa.

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (sabaq al-ḥadath): A situation in which a person's ablution becomes invalidated unexpectedly while they are engaged in prayer, requiring them to leave and perform wudu again.
البناء (al-binā'): Building upon the existing prayer by resuming from where one left off after performing wudu, without starting the entire prayer anew.
الاستئناف (al-isti'nāf): Starting the prayer completely from the beginning instead of building upon it after hadath.
الاستخلاف (al-istikhlāf): The imam appointing a substitute to lead the remainder of the prayer while he goes to perform wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
If an imam's ablution breaks during prayer, what is the correct Hanafi ruling?
A) He must immediately end the prayer and restart.
B) He may appoint a substitute, perform wudu, and build upon his prayer if he does not speak.
C) He must wait for his substitute to return before continuing.
D) He should cancel the prayer and lead a new one later.

Key Takeaway
Building upon prayer after hadath is allowed for imam, follower, and alone person under strict conditions of no speech or excess action; restarting is often preferred to avoid disagreement, except when preserving congregation is important.

Building vs. Starting Anew After Hadath in Prayer
Commentary on ruling for one who experiences hadath during prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling on bina and isti'naf after hadath for the solitary worshipper, imam, and follower, and identify when bina is preferred to preserve congregation.

Core Idea
Starting anew avoids disagreement, but building preserves the congregation's reward.

When a minor impurity occurs during prayer, the Hanafi school allows either building upon the previous prayer after wudu or starting anew. The commentator explains which option is better in different circumstances, considering the value of congregation and the desire to avoid scholarly disagreement. This lesson unpacks the rulings for the solitary worshipper, the follower, and the imam, highlighting the conditions that affect the preference.

Guided Path
1
Identify the base ruling and the two options
The base ruling: both bina (building) and isti'naf (starting anew) are valid after hadath. The commentator then discusses which is afdal (better). Locate the statement: 'wal-isti'naf afdal' and understand that this is the starting point.
The default preference is isti'naf to avoid shubhat al-khilaf.
2
Analyze the conditions for the solitary worshipper (munfarid)
For a person praying alone, the preferred view is isti'naf. However, some scholars say bina in the same place is better to minimize walking. Note the range of opinions.
The munfarid has flexibility; the key is avoiding unnecessary movement.
3
Examine the case of a follower (ma'mum) who experiences hadath
The follower leaves for wudu, then returns. If the imam is still praying and there is no barrier (hail), the follower may rejoin from his new location. If the imam has finished, he must build in his new location or start anew. Understand the conditions for returning to the original place.
The barrier (hail) could be a road or wall; its absence permits joining from the wudu spot.
4
Examine the case of an imam who experiences hadath
If the imam leaves for wudu, he loses his imamah and becomes a follower. A second person takes over as imam. If the original imam's prayer becomes invalid before the second leads, all followers' prayers are invalid. Note the critical point of timing.
The imam's departure from the mosque forfeits his leadership.
5
Apply the intra-Hanafi preference rule for congregation
Later scholars weigh the merit of congregation (fadilat al-jama'ah). If the imam and follower can find another congregation, isti'naf is better; if not, bina is better to preserve the congregation's reward. This tarjih is upheld in al-Fatawa.
The mufta bihi is bina when no other congregation is found.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام سبق الحدث

والاستئناف أفضل في مكان واحد.

وقيل : الأفضل في الموضع الذي توضأ فيه؛ لما فيه من تقليل المشي.

وأما إذا كان مقتدياً، فانصرف وتوضأ : فإنه يعود إلى مكانه، إلا أن يكون إمامه قد فرغ من صلاته، أو لا يكون بينهما حائل: فيجوز له الاقتداء به وهو في موضعه الذي توضأ فيه.

وإن كان الإمام قد فرغ: جاز له أن يبني على صلاته في الموضع الذي توضأ فيه.

وأما إذا كان إماماً، فانصرف وتوضأ، وعاد إلى مصلاه: صار مأموماً، والإمام هو الثاني ؛ لأنه لما خرج من المسجد : خرج من الإمامة، وصار مؤتماً.

ولو أن الإمام أفسد صلاته قبل أن يقوم الثاني مكانه: فسدت صلاتهم جميعاً.

قوله: (والاستئناف: أفضل)؛ تحرزاً عن شبهة الخلاف.

وهذا في حق الكل عند بعض المشايخ.

وقيل: هذا في حق المنفرد قطعاً، وأما الإمام والمأموم إن كانا يجدان جماعة: فالاستئناف أفضل أيضاً.

وإن كانا لا يجدان : فالبناء أفضلُ ؛ صيانةً لفضيلة الجماعة، وصحح هذا في «الفتاوى».
Rulings of Previous Hadath. And starting anew is better in one place. And it is said: the best is the place where he performed wudu; because of the reduction of walking. And as for if he is a follower, left and performed wudu: then he returns to his place, unless his imam has finished his prayer, or there is no barrier between them: then it is permissible for him to follow the imam while in his place where he performed wudu. And if the imam has finished: it is permissible for him to build on his prayer in the place where he performed wudu. And as for if he is an imam, left and performed wudu, and returned to his prayer place: he becomes a follower, and the imam is the second; because when he left the mosque, he left the imamate, and became a follower. And if the imam invalidated his prayer before the second (one) takes his place: then the prayer of all of them is invalid. His statement: (And starting anew: is better); to avoid the shade of disagreement. And this is in the right of all according to some shaykhs. And it is said: this is in the right of the individual absolutely, and as for the imam and follower, if they find a congregation: then starting anew is also better. And if they do not find (a congregation): then building is better; to protect the merit of congregation, and this was declared correct in al-Fatawa.
Source pages p. 407

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the ruling regarding one who experiences minor impurity (hadath) during prayer. The base ruling is that the person may either build upon the previous prayer (bina) by returning after wudu, or start anew (isti'naf). The text discusses the preferred option for different situations. For a person praying alone, starting anew is better in general, but some say it's better to return to the same place to minimize walking. For a follower who left to perform wudu, if the imam is still praying and there is no barrier, he can follow the imam from his new location; otherwise he must return. If the imam had finished, the follower can build in his new location. For an imam who left, he becomes a follower and a new imam takes over. If the original imam's prayer is invalidated before the second leads, all followers' prayers are invalid. The commentary clarifies that the preference for starting anew is to avoid the scholarly disagreement (shubhat al-khilaf). There is a difference of opinion among Hanafi scholars: some say this preference applies to all; others say only for the individual, while for the imam and follower, if they can find a congregation, starting anew is better, but if not, building is better to preserve the congregation's reward. The view that building is better for the congregation when no other congregation is found is upheld in later fatwa collections.

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (sabaq al-hadath): The occurrence of a minor impurity (hadath) during the prayer, requiring wudu.
بناء (bina): Building upon the previous prayer after removing the impurity, i.e., continuing from where one left off.
استئناف (isti'naf): Starting the prayer anew from the beginning.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) He must return to his original place.
B) He may follow the imam from his current location.
C) He must start his prayer anew.
D) He should wait for the imam to finish.

Key Takeaway
Starting anew avoids disagreement, but building preserves the congregation's reward when no other congregation is found.

Major Impairments and Speech in Prayer: Hanafi Rulings
Commentary on rulings for major impairments and speech in prayer.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings for each major impairment during prayer and explain why speech invalidates prayer whether intentional or forgetful.

Core Idea
Loud laughter breaks both wudu and prayer; any understood speech, even forgetful, invalidates prayer.

Prayer is a state of intimate connection with Allah, and certain events break that state more severely than others. This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira explains the rulings for rare major impairments (wet dream, looking with ejaculation, insanity, fainting, loud laughter) and for speech—whether intentional or forgetful. The Hanafi school uniquely holds that loud laughter nullifies both wudu and prayer, and that all understood speech invalidates the prayer, a position that differs from other schools.

Guided Path
1
Identify the acts and their rulings
List the five major impairments mentioned: wet dream, looking with ejaculation, insanity, fainting, and loud laughter. For each, the ruling is that both wudu and prayer must be renewed (i.e., the prayer is batil). Then note the ruling for speech: intentional or forgetful speech invalidates the prayer.
Loud laughter is treated like speech but with a stronger effect (breaks wudu).
2
Locate the dalil (proof)
The proof is rational—not a specific text. The author says these events are rare ('yanduru wujudiha') and therefore not included in the meaning of what the text came with (i.e., the permission to build upon minor hadath). The text implies that only events that frequently occur are excused. For laughter, the proof is that it is like speech, which invalidates prayer, and worse; so it must also break wudu.
The citation to al-Mabsut provides authoritative backing.
3
Trace the wajh al-dalalah (legal reasoning)
Understand the reasoning: The original textual ruling (nas) allowed building upon minor hadath because it is common. These major impairments are rare, so they are not analogous and do not receive the same leniency. For speech, the nas on intentional speech is extended to forgetful speech by analogy (qiyas) because the element of communication is present, and the prohibition of speech in prayer is clear.
The analogy for laughter: it is more obscene than speech, so it deserves a stronger ruling.
4
Note the ikhtilaf (scholarly disagreement)
Other schools (notably Shafi'i) differ: they hold that forgetful speech does not invalidate prayer, and that laughter does not break wudu unless it involves speaking. The passage does not elaborate, but the hanafi_position_box indicates this.
This ikhtilaf has practical consequences for fatwa.
5
Evaluate the Hanafi tarjih
The Hanafi position is mufta bihi within the school. The reliance on al-Mabsut (Zahir al-Riwayah) solidifies it. The reasoning is that speech is inherently incompatible with prayer, and laughter is even more so.
Later Hanafi works affirm this position.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله: (فإن نام فاحتلم أو نَظَرَ إلى امرأة فأنزل، أو جُنَّ، أو أغمي عليه، أو قهقه في الصلاة استأنف الوضوء والصلاة جميعاً). لأن هذه العوارض يندر وجودها في الصلاة، فلم تكن في معنى ما ورد به النص.

وكذا القهقهة؛ لأنها بمنزلة الكلام.

قال في «المبسوط» (۱): هي أفحش من الكلام عند المناجاة، حتى نقضت الوضوء، ثم سوى بين النسيان والعمد في الكلام، ففي القهقهة أولى.

قوله : (فإن تكلم في صلاته عامداً أو ساهياً: بطلت صلاته). يعني كلاماً يُعرف في متفاهم الناس، سواء حصلت به حروف، أم لا، حتى لو قال ما يُساق به الحمار: فسدت صلاته.

(۱) ۱۷۱/۱
His statement: (If he sleeps and has a wet dream, or looks at a woman and ejaculates, or becomes insane, or faints, or laughs loudly in prayer: he renews wudu and prayer altogether). Because these occurrences rarely happen in prayer, so they are not within the meaning of what the text (nas) came with. And likewise loud laughter; because it is like speech. He said in al-Mabsut: It is more obscene than speech during intimate conversation, such that it breaks wudu, then they made forgetfulness and intentional equal in case of speech, so in case of laughter it is more deserving. His statement: (If he speaks in his prayer intentionally or forgetfully: his prayer is invalid). That is, speech that is understood among people, whether it consists of letters or not, even if he says that which a donkey is driven with, his prayer becomes invalid.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage covers rulings when major impairments occur during prayer: sleeping with a wet dream, looking and ejaculating, insanity, fainting, and loud laughter. In all these cases, the person must renew both wudu (due to the hadath) and the prayer (because the prayer is invalidated). The reason given is that these events are rare, so they do not fall under the analogy of the textual ruling (which allowed building for minor hadath). Laughter is considered like speech but worse; in Hanafi fiqh, loud laughter breaks both wudu and prayer. The commentary from al-Mabsut explains that laughter is more obscene than speech during intimate conversation (munajat), so it breaks wudu, and since speech invalidates prayer whether intentional or forgetful, laughter does so even more. Regarding speech, the ruling is that intentional or forgetful speech invalidates the prayer. Speech is defined as understood communication, even if it does not form distinct letters, such as the sound used to drive a donkey.

Key Terms
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud laughter in prayer that invalidates both wudu and prayer.
كلام (kalam): Speech that is understood among people, whether it consists of letters or not, that invalidates prayer if uttered intentionally or forgetfully.
عوارض كبرى (awarid kubra): Major impairments that are rare and invalidate prayer and often require renewal of wudu.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling on loud laughter (qahqaha) during prayer?
A) It invalidates the prayer but not wudu.
B) It invalidates both wudu and prayer.
C) It only invalidates wudu.
D) It does not affect the prayer or wudu.

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, loud laughter invalidates both wudu and prayer; any understood speech, whether intentional or forgetful, invalidates the prayer.

Speech, Moaning, and Crying in Prayer: What Invalidates?
Commentary on matn ruling with exception and proofs.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling on speech invalidating prayer, explain the exception for crying from fear of Allah, and apply the distinction to moaning and sighing.

Core Idea
Speech invalidates prayer; but crying from fear of Allah is like dhikr and does not break it.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira comments on the Quduri matn regarding speech in prayer. It establishes that any intelligible utterance invalidates the prayer, but then carves out an important exception: crying, moaning, or sighing that arises from fear of Allah is not considered speech and does not invalidate. The author provides Quranic and Prophetic proofs to support this exception.

Guided Path
1
Identify the General Ruling
Start by noting the matn's ruling: speaking intentionally or forgetfully invalidates prayer. Understand that 'speech' includes any understood utterance, even without letters (e.g., sounds to drive animals).
This is a strict definition to preserve the sanctity of prayer.
2
Examine the Exception
Read the exception: moaning (anin), sighing (ta'awwuh), and crying (buka') that produce letters do not invalidate if due to fear of Allah (remembrance of Paradise or Hell). Why? Because it indicates increased humility and is akin to tasbih.
Contrast this with crying from worldly pain or calamity, which does invalidate.
3
Analyze the Proofs
Study the three proofs: (1) Quranic verse (17:109) praising those who weep in prostration, (2) Hadith that the Prophet's chest rumbled like a kettle from crying, (3) Narration that Umar sobbed audibly in prayer. These show that crying from fear of Allah is permissible and does not require repetition.
The proof is that these actions were done in prayer without renewal.
4
Apply the Distinction
Apply the principle: If the sound (letters) arises from worldly pain, it is 'speech of people' and invalidates. If from fear of Allah, it is like dhikr and valid. Distinguish moaning/sighing similarly.
The intention behind the sound determines the ruling.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
قوله : (فإن تكلم في صلاته عامداً أو ساهياً: بطلت صلاته). يعني كلاماً يُعرف في متفاهم الناس، سواء حصلت به حروف، أم لا، حتى لو قال ما يُساق به الحمار: فسدت صلاته. فإن أنَّ في صلاته أو تأوه أو بكى، فارتفع بكاؤه، أي حصل به حروف: فإن كان من ذكر الجنة أو النار : لم يضره؛ لأنه يدل على زيادة الخشوع، فكان في معنى التسبيح. والدليل على أن البكاء في الصلاة من خوف الله لا يقطع الصلاة: أن الله تعالى مَدَحَ على ذلك، فقال: ﴿ وَيَخِرُّونَ لِلْأَذْقَانِ يَبْكُونَ ) الإسراء/ ۱۰۹ ، أي يَخرون سجوداً على الوجوه يبكون، والمراد بالأذقان: الوجوه. وعن رسول الله صلى الله عليه وسلم أنه كان يصلي فيسمع لصدره أزيز كأزيز المرجل من البكاء (١). وعن عبد الله بن شداد قال: كنت أصلي خلف عمر رضي الله عنه صلاة الصبح، وكان يقرأ سورة يوسف، حتى إذا بلغ: ﴿ قَالَ إِنَّمَا أَشْكُوا بَنِي وَحُزْنِي إِلَى اللَّهِ .. يوسف / ٨٦ : سمعتُ نشيجه وأنا آخر الصفوف»(۲). الأزيز : غليان القدر، والمرجل: القدر. وإن كان من وجع أو مصيبة : قَطَعَ الصلاة؛ لأن فيه إظهار الجزع والتأسف ، فكان من كلام الناس.
He said: (If he speaks in his prayer intentionally or forgetfully: his prayer is invalidated). Meaning speech that is understood among people, whether it consists of letters or not, such that even if he says what is used to drive a donkey, his prayer is invalid. So if he moans in his prayer or sighs or cries, and his crying rises, i.e., letters are produced: if it is due to remembrance of Paradise or Hell, it does not harm him; because it indicates increased humility, so it is in the meaning of tasbih. And the proof that crying in prayer from fear of Allah does not cut the prayer is that Allah praised that, saying: 'And they fall down on their faces in prostration weeping' (17:109), meaning they fall down prostrating on their faces crying, and by 'chins' is meant faces. And from the Messenger of Allah ﷺ that he used to pray and his chest could be heard rumbling like the rumbling of a kettle from crying. And from Abdullah ibn Shaddad: I used to pray behind Umar رضي الله عنه in the dawn prayer, and he was reciting Surah Yusuf, until when he reached 'He said: I only complain of my grief and sorrow to Allah' (12:86), I heard his sobbing while I was in the last rows. Al-aziz: the boiling of the pot, and al-mirjal: the pot. And if it is from pain or calamity, it cuts the prayer; because it shows impatience and regret, so it is from the speech of people.
Source pages p. 408

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on the matn ruling that speaking in prayer, whether intentional or forgetful, invalidates the prayer. The key point is that 'speech' is defined as any intelligible utterance that people understand, regardless of whether it contains letters or not. Even making a sound used to drive a donkey (like 'sssh' or 'clucking') invalidates the prayer because it is meaningful. The text then addresses exceptions: moaning (أنين), sighing (تأوه), and crying (بكاء). If these produce letters (i.e., distinct sounds), they are normally invalidating speech. However, if the crying is from the fear of Allah, such as when remembering Paradise or Hell, it does not invalidate prayer because it indicates increased humility and is akin to tasbih (glorification). The author provides three proofs: (1) Quranic verse (17:109) praising those who weep in prostration; (2) Hadith that the Prophet's chest rumbled like a kettle from crying during prayer; (3) a narration that Umar ibn al-Khattab sobbed audibly while reciting Surah Yusuf. These show that crying out of fear of Allah is permissible and does not invalidate. Conversely, if the crying is due to worldly pain or calamity, it does invalidate because it expresses impatience and complaint, thus falling under 'speech of people.'

Key Terms
أنين (anin): moaning; a sound of pain or distress; if it produces letters and is from worldly pain, it invalidates; if from fear of Allah, not.
نشيجة (nashij): sobbing; audible crying with inhalation, as reported from Umar.
أزيز (aziz): rumbling sound like a boiling kettle; used to describe the sound of the Prophet's chest when crying.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
Which type of crying invalidates prayer according to the Hanafi school?
A) Crying from the fear of Allah
B) Crying from a worldly calamity
C) Crying while reciting Quran
D) Crying during prostration

Key Takeaway
Speech that is understood by people invalidates prayer; but sounds of devotion like crying from fear of Allah are valid and akin to dhikr.

Rulings on Sounds During Prayer: Groaning, Clearing Throat, Blowing Dust
Rulings with intra-Hanafi differences

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi rulings on groaning, clearing throat, and blowing dust during prayer, and identify the conditions that make these actions invalidate the prayer.

Core Idea
Deliberate production of letters without excuse invalidates prayer; necessity and unavoidability are excused.

This lesson examines three sounds that may occur during prayer: groaning from pain, clearing the throat, and blowing dust from the prostration spot. The Hanafi school distinguishes between actions that invalidate the prayer and those that are excused, based on intention and necessity.

Guided Path
1
Identify the action and the relevant Hanafi imam's view
For each sound (groaning, clearing throat, blowing dust), note the positions of Abu Hanifa, Muhammad, and Abu Yusuf as mentioned in the passage.
There are intra-Hanafi differences; focus on the majority view unless specified.
2
Determine if the action is voluntary or involuntary
The ruling depends on whether the person can refrain from the action. If involuntary (e.g., sneezing), it is excused.
3
Check if the action produces distinct letters
If the sound results in letters like 'ahh' or 'akh', it is considered speech-like and may invalidate if deliberate.
Isolated sounds without letters are usually excused.
4
Apply the exception for necessity
If the person is compelled (e.g., phlegm, illness, correcting recitation), the action is excused ('afw) and does not invalidate.
The Mabsut adds clearing to correct recitation as excused.
5
State the ruling
Combine the above: if deliberate, letter-producing, and without necessity, the prayer is invalidated; otherwise, it remains valid.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
أحكام سبق الحدث

21.
وعن أبي يوسف الأنينُ من الوجع إن كان يمكنه الامتناع منه : قَطَعَ الصلاة، وإلا فلا.
:
وعن محمد: إن كان المرض خفيفاً: يقطع الصلاة، وإلا فلا.
:
- وإن نفخ التراب عن موضع سجوده: إن كان غير مسموع: لا يُفسد، إجماعاً، وإن كان مسموعاً: أفسد عندهما.
وقال أبو يوسف: لا يُفسد.
وإن تنحنح لغير عذر بأن لم يكن مضطراً إليه، وحصل به حروف، نحو أخ أخ: بالفتح أو الضم ينبغي أن تفسد صلاته عند أبي حنيفة ومحمد.
وإن كان مضطراً، بأن اجتمع البلغم في حلقه: فهو عفو، كالعطاس لا يفسد الصلاة.
وفي المبسوط : إذا تنحنح لإصلاح القراءة: لا تفسد؛ لأنه حينئذ لا يمكنه الاحتراز عنه.
- وإن قبلت المصلي امرأته، ولم يُقبلها :هو : لا تفسد صلاته، وإن قبلها هو: فسدت صلاته.
وكذا لو كانت هي تصلي فقبلها: لا تفسد صلاتها.
Rulings of Preceding Hadath.

21. From Abu Yusuf: Groaning from pain—if he can refrain from it, it breaks the prayer, otherwise no.
From Muhammad: If the illness is light, it breaks the prayer, otherwise no.

- If he blows dust from his prostration place: if it is not audible, it does not invalidate, by consensus. If it is audible, it invalidates according to the two (Abu Hanifa and Muhammad). Abu Yusuf said: it does not invalidate.

If he clears his throat without an excuse, i.e., he is not compelled to do so, and letters are produced, like 'akh, akh' with fatha or damma—it should invalidate his prayer according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad.

If he is compelled, e.g., phlegm gathered in his throat, it is excused, like sneezing—it does not invalidate prayer.

In al-Mabsut: If he clears his throat to correct his recitation, it does not invalidate, because then he cannot avoid it.

- If the praying man kisses his wife and she does not kiss him: his prayer is not invalidated. If he kisses her, his prayer is invalidated.
Similarly, if she is praying and he kisses her: her prayer is not invalidated.
Source pages p. 410

Commentary
This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents rulings on various actions that may or may not invalidate prayer, based on the Hanafi school. The author begins with 'groaning from pain': according to Abu Yusuf, if the person can suppress the moan but does not, it breaks prayer; otherwise, it does not. Muhammad distinguishes by severity: a light illness where one can control still breaks prayer if done, but severe illness is excused. Next, blowing dust from the prostrations spot: if the sound is inaudible, all agree it does not invalidate; if audible, Abu Hanifa and Muhammad say it does, while Abu Yusuf disagrees. Clearing the throat (tanahnuh) is divided: without excuse and producing letters (like 'akh') invalidates according to Abu Hanifa and Muhammad; but if compelled by phlegm, it is like sneezing and excused. The Mabsut adds that clearing to correct recitation is excused because unavoidable. Finally, kissing: if the praying person initiates the kiss, his prayer breaks; if he is kissed, it does not. This distinction applies equally if the wife is praying.

Key Terms
أنين (anīn): Groaning or moaning from pain or illness
تنحنح (tanahnuh): Clearing the throat audibly
عفو (ʿafw): Excused; actions that do not invalidate prayer due to necessity or unavoidability

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling if a person praying clears his throat to correct his recitation?
A) The prayer is invalidated because any sound from clearing throat breaks the prayer.
B) The prayer is not invalidated because he cannot avoid it in that situation.
C) The prayer is invalidated only if he produces letters like 'akh'.
D) The prayer is invalidated according to all Hanafi imams.

Key Takeaway
A sound during prayer invalidates only if it is deliberate, produces letters, and lacks a valid excuse.

Kissing During Prayer: Who Initiates Matters
Ruling on kissing in prayer

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on kissing during prayer and explain why the initiator's prayer is invalidated while the recipient's prayer remains valid.

Core Idea
When a praying person initiates a kiss, his prayer invalidates; being kissed does not invalidate the recipient's prayer.

This lesson covers the ruling of kissing during prayer. The Hanafi school makes a clear distinction based on who initiates the kiss. If the person in prayer kisses his spouse, his prayer becomes void. However, if the spouse kisses the person in prayer, the prayer remains valid. This ruling applies symmetrically whether the praying person is a man or a woman.

Guided Path
1
Identify the actor
Determine who is performing the action: the person in prayer or the non-praying spouse.
2
Apply the ruling based on initiator
If the praying person initiates the kiss, the prayer is invalidated (fasad). If the non-praying person initiates, the prayer of the praying person remains valid.
The sex of the praying person does not matter; the same rule applies whether it is a man or a woman praying.
3
Understand the rationale
The kiss is an act that breaks the state of prayer (tahrimah) when done deliberately by the person in prayer. When done by another, it is not an action of the praying person, so it does not affect their prayer.
This is similar to the ruling on others touching or speaking to the praying person; only the praying person's own actions count.

Subq al-Hadath After Tashahhud and the Qahqaha Dispute
Rulings on subq al-hadath and qahqaha dispute

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when hadath occurs after tashahhud and explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of the Imam's qahqaha on masbuqun.

Core Idea
Hadath after tashahhud requires wudu for salam; the Imam's qahqaha invalidates masbuqun's prayer according to Abu Hanifa.

This lesson examines two interrelated rulings: first, what happens if a person breaks wudu after sitting for the final tashahhud; second, a detailed intra-Hanafi dispute about the effect of the Imam's loud laughter on latecomers. Al-Khujandi's commentary expands on five scenarios, showing consensus and disagreement.

Guided Path
1
Identify the basic rule for subq al-hadath after tashahhud
The text states that if hadath occurs after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, one must perform wudu and then say salam. This is because taslim is wajib and requires purity.
The rule applies whether the hadath is intentional or unintentional.
2
Understand the reason for the rule
The reasoning: the prayer's pillars are complete after tashahhud; only the wajib taslim remains. Hadath does not invalidate the entire prayer, but taslim cannot be performed without wudu. Therefore, wudu is necessary.
Intentional hadath or speaking also results in the prayer being complete—no rebuilding is possible.
3
Note the five scenarios from al-Khujandi
Al-Khujandi expands on the Imam's actions after tashahhud: qahqaha, intentional hadath, salam, speech, and standing. In three (salam, speech, standing), the prayers of all are complete by consensus. For qahqaha and intentional hadath, the Imam's prayer is complete, but there is disagreement about masbuqun.
The lahiqun (those who joined late but within the same rak'ah) are considered in the same status as the Imam.
4
Analyze the intra-Hanafi dispute on qahqaha
According to Abu Hanifa, the prayer of masbuqun is invalid because the qahqaha invalidates the portion of the Imam's prayer they encountered. Since the masbuq must build upon a valid part, and the encountered portion is invalid, his entire prayer becomes invalid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad presumably hold it valid, arguing that the masbuq's prayer is independent.
The practical difference: a masbuq who was present during the Imam's qahqaha must repeat his prayer according to Abu Hanifa, but not according to the Sahibayn.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وإن سبقه الحدث بعد ما قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التشهد : توضأ، وسلَّم.

قوله: (وإن سبقه الحدث بعد التشهد: توضأ وسلَّم)؛ لأن التسليم واجب، فلا بد من التوضئ ليأتي به.
* قوله : (وإن تعمد الحدث في هذه الحالة): أي بعد التشهد. * قوله : (أو تكلَّم ، أو عَمِلَ عملاً ينافي الصلاة: تمت صلاته)؛ لأنه تعذر البناء لوجود القاطع، ولم يبق عليه شيء من الأركان.
قال الخُجندي: الإمام إذا قهقه بعد ما قعد قدر التشهد، أو أحدث متعمداً وخلفه لاحقون ومسبوقون، فهذا على خمسة أوجه:
القهقهة والحدث العمد والسلام، والكلام، والقيام:
ففي ثلاثة منها: صلاة الكل تامة، في السلام، والقيام، والكلام، بالاتفاق.
وأما القهقهة، والحدث العمد فصلاة الإمام ومن هو بمثل حاله: تامة.
وأما صلاة المسبوقين : ففاسدة عند أبي حنيفة؛ لأن القهقهة مفسدة للجزء الذي تلاقيه من صلاة الإمام، فيفسد مثله من صلاة المقتدي، غير أن الإمام لا يحتاج إلى البناء، والمسبوق محتاج إليه، والبناء على الفاسد: فاسد.
And if hadath precedes him after he has sat for the duration of the tashahhud: he performs wudu and says salam.

His saying: (And if hadath precedes him after tashahhud: he performs wudu and says salam) because the taslim is wajib, so he must perform wudu to do it.
*His saying: (and if he intentionally creates hadath in this state): i.e., after tashahhud. *His saying: (or speaks, or does an act that contradicts prayer: his prayer is complete) because building upon it is impossible due to the invalidator, and no pillars remain upon him.

Al-Khujandi said: If the Imam laughs loudly after sitting for the duration of tashahhud, or intentionally has a hadath, and behind him are lahiqun and masbuqun, then this has five aspects:
Qahqaha, intentional hadath, salam, speech, and standing:
In three of them, the prayer of all is complete: salam, standing, and speech, by agreement.
As for qahqaha and intentional hadath, the prayer of the Imam and whoever is in his same situation is complete.
As for the prayer of the masbuqun: it is invalid according to Abu Hanifa; because qahqaha invalidates the part of the Imam's prayer that they encountered, so it invalidates the like from the follower's prayer, except that the Imam does not need to rebuild, while the masbuq needs to rebuild, and building upon an invalid (foundation) is invalid.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage addresses a scenario where a person breaks his wudu (hadath) after having sat for the duration of the tashahhud (the final sitting). The rule is: he must perform a new wudu and then say the salam. This is because taslim is wajib and is part of the prayer, so it requires purity. If he intentionally breaks wudu, or speaks, or does any act that invalidates prayer, his prayer is considered complete (he does not need to repeat it) because he has already fulfilled all the pillars before the invalidator, and building upon the prayer after an invalidator is impossible. Then the commentary by al-Khujandi discusses a situation where the Imam laughs loudly (qahqaha) or intentionally breaks wudu after tashahhud, while there are latecomers (lahiqun and masbuqun) behind him. Five aspects are considered: qahqaha, intentional hadath, salam, speech, and standing. In three (salam, speech, standing), everyone's prayer is complete by consensus. For qahqaha and intentional hadath, the Imam's prayer and those in his same situation (like the muqtadi who are also at the same stage) are complete. However, according to Abu Hanifa, the prayer of the masbuqun (those who missed some rak'ahs) is invalid. The reason: the qahqaha invalidates the part of the Imam's prayer that the masbuq encountered; thus the masbuq's prayer is corrupted because he must build his remaining prayer upon a valid part, and building upon an invalid part makes the whole invalid. This is an intra-Hanafi dispute: Abu Hanifa holds the masbuq's prayer invalid, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad presumably hold it valid (though not stated explicitly here, the text implies agreement on the other three aspects).

Key Terms
سبق الحدث (subq al-hadath): The occurrence of an event that breaks wudu before the completion of the prayer
قعد قدر التشهد (qa'ada qadr al-tashahhud): Sat for the duration required to recite the tashahhud
قهقهة (qahqaha): Loud, forced laughter that produces sounds with letters
لاحق (lahiq): A latecomer who joined after the Imam's ruku' but within the same rak'ah
مسبوق (masbuq): One who missed one or more full rak'ahs of the congregational prayer

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, what is the ruling regarding the prayer of masbuqun (latecomers) if the Imam laughs loudly (qahqaha) after sitting for tashahhud?
A) Their prayer is complete like the Imam's.
B) Their prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa.
C) Their prayer is invalid according to all imams.
D) Their prayer is valid only if they also laugh.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, hadath does not invalidate the prayer entirely; only wudu is needed for salam. The Imam's qahqaha after tashahhud invalidates the prayer of masbuqun according to Abu Hanifa, due to the need for a valid foundation.

Rulings on Hadath After Tashahhud
States rulings when hadath occurs after sitting amount of tashahhud

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the ruling when hadath occurs after tashahhud in prayer, distinguishing between unintentional and deliberate cases, and identify the consequence for each.

Core Idea
A deliberate hadath after tashahhud completes the prayer; an unintentional one requires wudu and taslim.

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyira clarifies what a praying person must do if they experience a hadath (breaking of wudu) after sitting for the amount of tashahhud. The ruling depends on whether the hadath was unintentional or deliberate. Understanding this distinction ensures the prayer is completed correctly and avoids unnecessary repetition or invalidation.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its timing
Determine that the hadath occurs after the person has sat for the duration of tashahhud in the last rak'ah. This timing is crucial because at that point only the wajib of taslim remains.
Tashahhud is the sitting and recitation of the testimony of faith.
2
Differentiate between unintentional and deliberate
The ruling changes based on whether the hadath was intentional (deliberate) or unintentional (e.g., caused by a sudden event beyond control).
3
Apply ruling for unintentional hadath
If unintentional, the person must perform wudu (or tayammum if water is unavailable) and then say taslim. This is because taslim is wajib and requires ritual purity.
The prayer is not invalidated; only wudu is needed to complete the wajib.
4
Apply ruling for deliberate hadath
If the person deliberately causes the hadath, or speaks or performs any action that contradicts the prayer, the prayer is considered complete (tammat). No further action is needed.
The deliberate act cuts off the prayer, and since no rukn remains, the prayer is valid.
5
Understand the rationale
The rationale is that after tashahhud, only the wajib of taslim remains. For unintentional hadath, wudu is required to perform it. For deliberate invalidation, the prayer ends because building upon it is impossible due to the 'cutter' (qati').

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
وَإِنْ سَبَقَهُ الْحَدَثُ بَعْدَ مَا قَعَدَ قَدْرَ التَّشَهُّدِ : تَوَضَّأَ، وَسَلَّمَ. وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هٰذِهِ الْحَالَةِ، أَوْ تَكَلَّمَ، أَوْ عَمِلَ عَمَلًا يُنَافِي الصَّلَاةَ : تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَإِنْ سَبَقَهُ الْحَدَثُ بَعْدَ التَّشَهُّدِ: تَوَضَّأَ وَسَلَّمَ)؛ لِأَنَّ التَّسْلِيمَ وَاجِبٌ، فَلَا بُدَّ مِنَ التَّوَضُّئِ لِيَأْتِيَ بِهِ. قَوْلُهُ: (وَإِنْ تَعَمَّدَ الْحَدَثَ فِي هٰذِهِ الْحَالَةِ): أَيْ بَعْدَ التَّشَهُّدِ. قَوْلُهُ: (أَوْ تَكَلَّمَ، أَوْ عَمِلَ عَمَلًا يُنَافِي الصَّلَاةَ: تَمَّتْ صَلَاتُهُ)؛ لِأَنَّهُ تَعَذَّرَ الْبِنَاءُ لِوُجُودِ الْقَاطِعِ، وَلَمْ يَبْقَ عَلَيْهِ شَيْءٌ مِنَ الْأَرْكَانِ.
And if the event preceded him after he sat the amount of tashahhud: he performs wudu and says taslim. And if he deliberately commits the event in this state, or speaks, or does an action that contradicts prayer: his prayer is complete. His statement: (And if the event preceded him after tashahhud: he performs wudu and says taslim) because taslim is obligatory, so wudu is necessary to perform it. His statement: (And if he deliberately commits the event in this state): that is, after tashahhud. His statement: (or speaks, or does an action that contradicts prayer: his prayer is complete) because building is prevented due to the existence of the cutter, and nothing of the pillars remains upon him.
Source pages p. 411

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn with commentary. It addresses what happens when a person performing prayer experiences a hadath (event that breaks wudu) after sitting for the amount of tashahhud. If it is unintentional, he must perform wudu and then say taslim, because taslim is wajib and cannot be performed without wudu. However, if he deliberately causes the hadath, or speaks, or performs any action that contradicts prayer (like excessive movement), then his prayer is considered complete (tammat) and he does not need to do anything further. The reason given is that since he introduced a deliberate invalidator (qati'), it is impossible to build upon the prayer, and no rukn remains to be performed. This ruling highlights the Hanafi position that the prayer ends with the obligation of taslim, and once the tashahhud is done, only the wajib of taslim remains.

Key Terms
التشهد (al-tashahhud): The sitting in the last rak'ah of prayer where the testimony of faith is recited.
الحدث (al-hadath): An event that nullifies ritual purity (wudu), such as passing wind, urination, etc.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
What must a person do if an unintentional hadath occurs after sitting the amount of tashahhud?
A) The prayer is invalid, and he must repeat it.
B) He performs wudu and then says taslim.
C) He ignores it and finishes the prayer.
D) He performs tayammum and continues.

Key Takeaway
After tashahhud, unintentional hadath requires wudu then taslim; deliberate hadath completes the prayer.
