The Effect of Missed Witr on Fajr Prayer
Ruling on validity of Fajr prayer if Witr missed

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of Fajr prayer when Witr is missed, and identify the mufta bihi view.

Core Idea
Witr is wajib and order matters for Abu Hanifa; the disciples say Fajr stands independent.

This lesson examines a case where a person prays Fajr while remembering that they haven't performed the Witr prayer. The Hanafi school has an internal difference: does the missed Witr invalidate the Fajr? Understanding this dispute clarifies the Hanafi view on the obligation of tartib (order) between prayers and the practical concession at the end of time.

Guided Path
1
State the scenario
Identify the situation: a person prays Fajr at its proper time, but at the time of prayer, he remembers that he has not yet performed the Witr prayer of the previous night.
The person is conscious of the missed Witr during the Fajr prayer.
2
Identify Abu Hanifa's ruling and exception
Abu Hanifa holds the Fajr prayer to be invalid (fasid) because the obligation of tartib (order) between Witr and Fajr is violated. However, he makes an exception: if the Fajr prayer is offered at the very end of its time, then it is valid, because the necessity of performing Fajr within its time outweighs the tartib requirement.
Tartib is a wajib element in prayers of the same category; breaking it deliberately invalidates the later prayer.
3
Identify the disciples' ruling
Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two disciples) rule that the Fajr prayer is complete and valid. They consider the missed Witr a separate obligation, and the validity of Fajr does not depend on having performed Witr beforehand.
This view is considered more practical and is from the zahir al-riwayah.
4
Understand the underlying principle
The dispute revolves around the principle of tartib (order) in prayers. Abu Hanifa views tartib as a condition for validity when the missed prayer is wajib and one remembers it during the later prayer. The disciples see no such condition affecting the later prayer if it is performed correctly on its own.
Tartib applies between fard and fard, and between fard and wajib according to Abu Hanifa.
5
Determine the mufta bihi
Later Hanafi scholars (e.g., in al-Hidayah) have favored the view of the two disciples, making it the relied-upon (mufta bihi) position for fatwa. Thus, in practice, one's Fajr prayer is valid even if Witr was missed, and the Witr should be made up later.
This is the practical ruling that students should apply.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو صلى الفجر وهو ذاكر أنه لم يوتر: فصلاة الفجر فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة، إلا أن يكون صلى الفجر في آخر وقتها. وعندهما: صلاة الفجر تامة.
And if he prays Fajr while remembering that he has not performed Witr, then the Fajr prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifah, unless he prayed Fajr at its very end. According to the two (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the Fajr prayer is complete.
Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the effect of a missed Witr prayer on a subsequent Fajr prayer. Witr is considered wajib in the Hanafi school, and there is an order (tartib) between Witr and Fajr, as Fajr comes after Witr. If a person prays Fajr while remembering that Witr was not performed, Abu Hanifa rules that the Fajr prayer is invalid because the tartib is violated, unless the Fajr was offered at the very end of its time, at which point the obligation of tartib is dropped due to necessity. The two disciples (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad) hold that the Fajr prayer is still valid, because the missed Witr is a separate obligation and does not nullify a properly performed Fajr. The relied-upon view is that of the two disciples, as it is more practical and allows the Fajr to count.

Key Terms
وتر (witr): The single (or three) rak'ah prayer performed after 'Isha; wajib in the Hanafi school.
فاسد (fasid): Invalid in the sense that the prayer does not fulfill the obligation and must be repeated.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the relied-upon view is that Fajr prayer remains valid even if one remembers missing Witr, and the Witr should be made up separately.

The Hanafi Ruling on an Unknown Missed Prayer
Ruling on unknown missed prayer with tartib conditions

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to apply the Hanafi ruling for an unknown missed prayer and explain how the obligation of order (tartib) is affected by constriction and forgetfulness.

Core Idea
When uncertain which prayer was missed, the Hanafi school requires repeating all five prayers of that day as a precaution.

In this passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, the commentator addresses a common scenario: a person knows that one obligatory prayer from a specific day has been missed, but cannot recall which one. The Hanafi school provides a precise method to fulfill the obligation without falling into doubt, based on the principle of ihtiyat (precaution). Additionally, the passage clarifies the status of order (tartib) in make-up prayers under conditions of constriction and forgetfulness.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The act is making up missed prayers (qada' al-fawa'it). The Hanafi school holds that qada' is wajib for every missed fard prayer. In this passage, the focus is on when the missed prayer is unknown.
The ruling is wajib, not fard, because the obligation is derived from a hadith with zanni thubut, though the practice is unanimously required.
2
Understand the role of tartib (order)
Tartib means performing missed prayers in the order they were missed. The passage explains that tartib is wajib in qada', but it drops in cases of constriction (diq) and is excused (not dropped) in forgetfulness. If the excuse ceases during the prayer, tartib returns.
Constriction refers to limited time that would cause a current prayer to expire if order is maintained.
3
Apply the ruling for an unknown missed prayer
If a person misses one prayer of a day and night and has no predominant opinion, he repeats all five prayers of that day as a precaution. If he has a predominant opinion, he acts on it.
This is based on ihtiyat (precaution) due to the uncertainty.
4
Compare with alternative views
The passage quotes Al-Thawri (pray Maghrib, Fajr, then four rak'ahs for the remaining three) and Bishr al-Marisi (pray four rak'ahs with three sittings). These differ from the Hanafi position.
The Hanafi view is that only full repetition of all five prayers ensures certainty.

Chapter of Making Up Missed Prayers: [if he prays it] in its time, then it is better. Source pages p. 425

Commentary
This passage begins by discussing the status of order (tartib) in making up missed prayers. The earlier context explains that if one prays a prayer in its time, it is better. When in a state of constriction (e.g., near the end of time), the obligation of order for that prayer is dropped. Once dropped in a specific prayer, it does not return for that same prayer. In contrast, forgetfulness does not drop the obligation of order; instead, the person is excused due to ignorance. If the excuse (ignorance) ceases before the prayer is complete, the obligation of order returns because the excuse is treated as if it never existed. The main ruling concerns a person who misses one prayer from a day and night but cannot identify which one. The Hanafi position is that as a precaution, he should repeat all five prayers of a day and night if he has no predominant opinion. If he has a strong guess, he prays according to that guess. The text then mentions two other opinions: Al-Thawri says to pray Maghrib, Fajr, and then four rak'ahs intending the remaining three (since Dhuhr, 'Asr, and 'Isha' all have four rak'ahs). Bishr al-Marisi says to pray four rak'ahs with three sittings, intending to cover any of the missed prayers due to the nature of transition between prayers.

Key Terms
قضاء الفوائت (qada' al-fawa'it): The chapter title referring to the rules of making up missed obligatory prayers (fara'id).
الترتيب (al-tartib): The obligation of performing missed prayers in the order they were missed (e.g., first Fajr, then Dhuhr, etc.).
الضيق (al-diqiq (constriction)): A situation where time is limited, such that performing the prayer in order would cause the time for a current prayer to expire.
الاحتياط (al-ihtiyat): The precautionary principle applied when uncertain, leading to repeating a full set of prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi position, what should a person do if he misses one prayer from a day and night and has a strong predominant opinion that it was Dhuhr?
A) Pray all five prayers to be safe.
B) Pray only Dhuhr, following his predominant opinion.
C) Pray Dhuhr and 'Asr because they both have four rak'ahs.
D) Pray four rak'ahs with the intention of covering all possibilities.

Key Takeaway
When the missed prayer is unknown and the person has no predominant opinion, the Hanafi school obligates repeating all five prayers of that day as a precautionary measure to ensure the obligation is fulfilled.

Fajr Validity When Remembering Missed Witr
Intra-Hanafi dispute on validity of Fajr when mindful of missed Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to distinguish between Abu Hanifa's and the Sahibayn's rulings on the validity of Fajr when mindful of missed Witr and explain the underlying cause (Witr's status).

Core Idea
The validity of Fajr when remembering missed Witr depends on whether Witr is wajib (Abu Hanifa) or sunnah (Sahibayn).

This passage from Al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah presents a clear intra-Hanafi dispute between Abu Hanifa and his two disciples regarding the effect of a missed Witr on the Fajr prayer. The disagreement is rooted in a more fundamental difference: the legal status of Witr itself. Understanding this dispute sharpens your ability to trace how a single usul principle—the classification of an act as wajib versus sunnah—can generate entirely different furu' rulings.

Guided Path
1
State the Hanafi Imams' positions
Identify the ruling of Abu Hanifa and the Sahibayn on the validity of Fajr when one remembers missing Witr before praying Fajr.
Abu Hanifa: Fajr is invalid unless at the very end of its time. Sahibayn: Fajr is valid.
2
Trace the basis of the dispute
Recognize that the difference stems from the legal status of Witr: Abu Hanifa holds it wajib; the Sahibayn hold it sunnah.
This is the key usul point that determines whether tartib (order) is required.
3
Analyze the tartib requirement
Apply the Hanafi principle: tartib is required between two fard/wajib prayers, but not between a fard and a sunnah.
Abu Hanifa: Witr is wajib, so tartib with Fajr (fard) is required, making Fajr invalid if Witr is missed. Sahibayn: Witr is sunnah, so no tartib, Fajr valid.
4
Note the exception
Abu Hanifa makes an exception: if one prays Fajr at the very end of its time (when performing Witr would cause Fajr to be missed), then Fajr is valid.
The requirement of tartib is waived due to time constriction.
5
Determine the thamarah al-khilaf
Identify the practical consequence: under Abu Hanifa's view, Fajr must be repeated (unless end of time); under the Sahibayn's view, no repetition is needed.
This difference affects actual practice for a person who remembers the missed Witr.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولو صلى الفجر وهو ذاكر أنه لم يوتر: فصلاة الفجر فاسدة عند أبي حنيفة، إلا أن يكون صلى الفجر في آخر وقتها.
وعندهما: صلاة الفجر تامة.
وهذا مبني على اختلافهم في الوتر، فعنده: لما كان واجباً: كان الترتيب شرطاً، وعندهما كان سنةً، فلا ترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن.
ثم عند أبي حنيفة: إذا فسد فرض الفجر: هل تفسد سنته؟
قال في «المستصفى»: لا تفسد.
وقد صرح به في المنظومة»(۱): فقال:
والوتر فرض ويرى بذكره في فجره فسادَ فَرْضِ فَجْرِه فقيد بفساد الفرض خاصةً، والله أعلم.
And if he prays Fajr while he remembers that he has not performed Witr, then the Fajr prayer is invalid according to Abu Hanifa, unless he prayed Fajr at the very end of its time. According to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), the Fajr prayer is complete. This is based on their difference regarding Witr: For him (Abu Hanifa), since Witr is wajib, the order (tartib) is a condition; for them, it is sunnah, so there is no order between obligations and sunnahs. Then, according to Abu Hanifa: if the Fajr fard becomes invalid, does its sunnah become invalid? He said in 'al-Mustasfa': it does not become invalid. And it is stated in 'al-Manzuma': 'And Witr is fard, and he holds that remembering it invalidates only the fard of Fajr.' So it is restricted to the invalidity of the fard specifically, and Allah knows best.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage presents an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the validity of the Fajr prayer when the person remembers that he has not yet prayed Witr (the Witr prayer) and still proceeds with Fajr. Abu Hanifa rules that the Fajr fard prayer is invalid (fasid) because he holds that Witr is wajib (obligatory), and therefore there is a requirement of order (tartib) between the missed wajib (Witr) and the subsequent fard (Fajr). However, he makes an exception: if the person prays Fajr at the very end of its time (when performing Witr would cause Fajr to be missed), then Fajr is valid. Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold that Fajr remains valid (tammah) because in their view Witr is sunnah, not wajib, so there is no requirement of order between a sunnah and a fard. The text further explains a secondary issue: According to Abu Hanifa, even if the fard of Fajr is invalid due to this, the sunnah prayer of Fajr (the two rak'ahs before Fajr) remains valid. This is clarified by a quote from 'al-Mustasfa' and a poetic line from 'al-Manzuma' by Najm al-Din al-Nasafi, which explicitly states that only the fard of Fajr is invalidated, not the sunnah.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The Witr prayer, a prayer performed after the night prayers, its status is disputed within the Hanafi school (wajib vs sunnah).
واجب (wajib): In Hanafi terminology, a legal obligation established by a zanni (probable) evidence, ranking below fard. Here, Abu Hanifa considers Witr as wajib, requiring order with fard.
سنة (sunnah): Recommended but not obligatory; the Sahibayn consider Witr as sunnah, thus no requirement of order with fard.
الترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن (al-tartib bayna al-fara'id wa al-sunan): The obligation of performing obligatory (fard) and wajib prayers in a specific order when making up missed prayers.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) If he performs Witr before Fajr.
B) If he prays Fajr at the very end of its time.
C) If he prays the sunnah of Fajr first.
D) If he is ignorant of the ruling.

Key Takeaway
The validity of Fajr when remembering missed Witr hinges on the legal status of Witr (wajib vs sunnah) within the Hanafi school.

Intra-Hanafi Dispute on Witr and Tartib in Missed Prayers
Explaining the basis of tartib on the status of Witr

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain why Abu Hanifa's view that Witr is wajib leads to tartib being a condition, while the Sahibayn's view that Witr is sunnah does not require tartib between fard and sunnah, and apply the mufta bihi ruling to a missed prayer scenario.

Core Idea
The entire ruling on tartib in making up missed prayers depends on whether Witr is wajib or sunnah.

This passage examines the foundational dispute among the Hanafi imams regarding the status of Witr prayer and how it shapes the rules for making up missed prayers. The commentator shows that the difference is not merely theoretical but has direct practical consequences for the order (tartib) between missed obligatory prayers and current prayers.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two positions on Witr
Recognize that Abu Hanifa holds Witr is wajib, while Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the Sahibayn) hold it is sunnah mu'akkadah. This difference is the root of the dispute.
The Arabic text uses 'عنده' for Abu Hanifa and 'عندهما' for the two companions.
2
Trace the legal consequence for tartib
Determine the ruling on order (tartib) when making up missed prayers. For Abu Hanifa, tartib becomes a condition (shart) because Witr is wajib; for the Sahibayn, no tartib is required between fard and sunnah prayers.
The key phrase: 'فكان الترتيب شرطا' vs 'فلا ترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن'.
3
Examine the subsidiary question on Fajr
Analyze the follow-up ruling: if the fard of Fajr becomes invalid, does its sunnah also become invalid? The text answers no, citing al-Mustasfa and al-Manzumah.
This shows the independence of sunnah from fard in invalidation.
4
Identify the thamarah al-khilaf
Note the practical consequence: a Hanafi following the mufta bihi must observe tartib when missed prayers are five or less, meaning they must make up missing prayers in order before praying the current prayer.
The Sahibayn's view would permit praying the current prayer first.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب قضاء الفوائت
وهذا مبني على اختلافهم في الوتر، فعنده: لما كان واجباً: كان الترتيب شرطاً، وعندهما كان سنةً، فلا ترتيب بين الفرائض والسنن.
ثم عند أبي حنيفة : إذا فسد فرض الفجر : هل تفسد سنته؟
قال في «المستصفى»: لا تفسد.
وقد صرح به في المنظومة»(۱): فقال:

(۱) منظومة نجم الدين النسفي المنظومة في الخلافيات) ص ٤٥.
Chapter: Making Up Missed Prayers
And this is based on their difference regarding Witr: according to him (Abu Hanifa), because it is obligatory, order is a condition; according to them (Abu Yusuf and Muhammad), because it is sunnah, there is no order between obligatory and sunnah prayers.
Then according to Abu Hanifa: if the obligatory Fajr prayer becomes invalid, does its sunnah become invalid?
He said in al-Mustasfa: It does not become invalid.
And it was explicitly stated in al-Manzumah: "Witr is obligatory, and he holds that by mentioning the invalidity of the obligatory Fajr prayer, the invalidity is restricted to the obligatory specifically." And Allah knows best.
(1) Manzumah of Najm al-Din al-Nasafi, al-Manzumah fi al-Khilafiyyat, p. 45.
Source pages p. 426

Commentary
This passage is an intra-Hanafi dispute regarding the ruling on making up missed prayers. The commentator explains that the entire discussion is built upon the difference of opinion among the Hanafi imams regarding the status of Witr prayer. According to Abu Hanifa, Witr is wajib (obligatory), therefore when making up missed prayers, order (tartib) must be observed between the missed prayers and the current prayer; meaning one cannot pray a current prayer before making up the missed ones in order. According to Abu Yusuf and Muhammad (the two companions, Sahibayn), Witr is sunnah (recommended), not wajib, so there is no requirement of order between obligatory prayers and sunnah prayers—one can pray the current prayer without making up missed ones first. The commentator then raises a subsidiary question: If one's fard (obligatory) Fajr prayer becomes invalid (e.g., due to a nullifier), does its associated sunnah (the two rak'ahs before Fajr) also become invalid? He quotes from al-Mustasfa that the sunnah does not become invalid. He also cites al-Manzumah (a poem on points of difference) by Najm al-Din al-Nasafi, which states that Witr is obligatory and that the invalidity mentioned in the verse (?) is restricted to the obligatory prayer specifically, not the sunnah. The passage thus clarifies the Hanafi positions on tartib (order) in qada' and the independence of sunnah from fard in invalidation.

Key Terms
الوتر (al-witr): The odd-numbered prayer performed after the night prayer (Isha), consisting of an odd number of rak'ahs, typically three.
الترتيب (al-tartib): Order; the condition that when making up missed prayers (fawā'it), one must perform them in their chronological order (e.g., missed Fajr before Zuhr, etc.).
الفرائض والسنن (al-farā'id wa al-sunan): Obligatory prayers (fard) and supererogatory prayers (sunnah); in this context, the difference in ruling on order between them.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because Witr is considered sunnah.
B) Because Witr is considered wajib.
C) Because Fajr prayer is obligatory.
D) Because of consensus (ijma).

Key Takeaway
In the Hanafi school, the requirement of tartib in making up missed prayers hinges on the dispute over the status of Witr: Abu Hanifa's view (Witr wajib) is the mufta bihi, making tartib a condition.

Placement and Titling of the Chapter on Disliked Prayer Times
Explaining the placement and titling of the chapter

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to explain the reasons behind the placement and titling of the chapter on disliked prayer times in al-Jawhara al-Nayyira, and distinguish between karaha and ʿadam al-jawāz in Hanafi fiqh.

Core Idea
Karaha is broader than ʿadam al-jawāz: every non-permissible act is disliked, but not every disliked act is non-permissible.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyira discusses two editorial decisions made by the author: where to place the chapter on disliked prayer times and what to title it. The commentator provides methodological justifications rooted in Hanafi legal theory, clarifying that karaha (dislike) is a more general category than ʿadam al-jawāz (non-permissibility).

Guided Path
1
Identify the two issues: placement and titling
The passage addresses two distinct questions: why the chapter is placed after the chapter on missed prayers, and why it is titled 'karaha' instead of 'ʿadam al-jawāz'.
2
Analyze the placement rationale
The commentator says karaha is a ʿāriḍ (incidental ruling) similar to fawāt (missing a prayer), so the two chapters are homogeneous. This justifies placing them together.
3
Contrast with al-Hidayah's placement
Al-Hidayah places the disliked times after the recommended times to give a complete picture of permissible and impermissible times. The commentator notes this alternative.
4
Analyze the titling rationale
Two reasons are given: (a) most rulings in the chapter are about disliked (makruh) times, not strictly non-permissible; (b) karaha is a more general term that includes both disliked and non-permissible acts.
5
Understand the analogy with bayʿ fāsid
Just as the term 'invalid sale' (bayʿ fāsid) in Hanafi terminology covers both invalid (fāsid) and void (bātil) sales, 'karaha' covers both disliked and non-permissible acts.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة
كان الأولى أن يذكر هذا الباب في باب المواقيت، كما في «الهداية» (١) ، وإنما ذكره هنا ؛ لأن الكراهة من العوارض، فأشبه الفوات، فتجانس البابان.
وحجة صاحب «الهداية»: أنه لما ذكر الأوقات التي تُستحب فيها الصلاة: عقبه بذكر ما يقابله من الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة؛ ليتمكن المصلي من صلاته بغير كراهة تقع في صلاته من جانب الوقت. - وإنما لقب الباب بالكراهة، ثم بدأ بعدم الجواز؛ لأنه اعتبر الأغلب، والمكروه أكثر من عدم الجواز.
أو لأن الكراهة أعم من عدم الجواز ؛ لأن كل ما لا يجوز: فالكراهة فيه حاصلة أيضاً، كما هي ثابتة في المكروه، ولا يلزم من كل مكروه: أنه لا يجوز، فالكراهة ثابتةٌ في الصورتين، وليس عدم الجواز ثابتاً في الكراهة.
وهذه التسمية : مثل تسمية البيع الفاسد وإن انخرط فيه البيع الباطل.
(1) إشارة إلى الهداية للمرغيناني.
Chapter: Times in Which Prayer is Disliked
It would have been more appropriate to mention this chapter in the chapter on prayer times, as in al-Hidayah (1). Rather, he mentioned it here because dislike (karaha) is among incidental rulings, so it resembles missing (fawāt), thus the two chapters are homogeneous.
The argument of the author of al-Hidayah: When he mentioned the times in which prayer is recommended, he followed it by mentioning the opposite, i.e., the times in which prayer is disliked, so that the worshiper can perform his prayer without any dislike occurring in his prayer due to the time. - And he titled the chapter with 'dislike' (karaha), then began with 'non-permissibility' because he considered the majority, and the disliked (makruh) is more than the non-permissible.
Or because 'dislike' is more general than 'non-permissibility'; for everything that is not permissible, dislike is also present in it, just as it is established in the disliked, and from every disliked thing it does not necessarily follow that it is not permissible. So dislike is established in both cases, while non-permissibility is not established in the disliked.
And this naming is like naming the invalid sale (al-bay' al-fāsid) even though it includes the void sale (al-bay' al-bāṭil).
(1) Reference to al-Hidayah by al-Marghinani.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a methodological explanation of why the author chose to place the chapter on disliked times for prayer after the chapter on making up missed prayers, rather than in the chapter on prayer times as in al-Hidayah. The commentator justifies this placement by noting that dislike (karaha) is an incidental ruling (ʿāriḍ) that affects the validity of prayer due to external factors, similar to fawāt (missing a prayer), so the two topics are naturally connected. He then contrasts this with the approach of al-Hidayah, which places the disliked times after the recommended times to create a complete picture for the worshiper. Next, the commentator addresses the titling of the chapter: although the chapter is titled 'karaha' (dislike), the author begins by discussing non-permissible times (ʿadam al-jawāz). He gives two possible reasons: either because the majority of the rulings in this chapter are about disliked times (makruh) rather than strictly impermissible, or because karaha is a broader term that includes both what is disliked and what is non-permissible. He explains that every non-permissible act is also disliked, but not every disliked act is non-permissible; thus, karaha covers both categories, making it the more appropriate title. He draws an analogy with the term 'invalid sale' (bayʿ fāsid), which in Hanafi terminology includes both void (bāṭil) and invalid (fāsid) sales, even though they are distinct. This clarifies the Hanafi legal usage of these terms.

Key Terms
الكراهة (al-karāhah): Dislike; a ruling that an act is detested but not necessarily prohibited. In this context, it is used as a generic term covering both makruh tahrimi (close to haram) and makruh tanzihi (lightly disliked).
عدم الجواز (ʿadam al-jawāz): Non-permissibility; the ruling that an act is not allowed, i.e., either haram or makruh tahrimi? In this text, it is contrasted with karaha as a narrower category (only the strictly impermissible).
العوارض (al-ʿawāriḍ): Incidental rulings or circumstances that affect the original ruling of an act, e.g., the time of day affecting the permissibility of prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) Because non-permissibility is more common in this chapter.
B) Because karaha is a broader term that includes both disliked and non-permissible acts.
C) Because the chapter only covers disliked (makruh) times.
D) Because the author made an error and later corrected it.

Key Takeaway
The title 'karaha' is chosen because it encompasses both disliked and non-permissible acts, just as 'bayʿ fāsid' includes both invalid and void sales.

Prohibited Prayer Times: Sunrise, Midday, Sunset
Explains the ruling and scope of prohibited prayer times

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer during the three prohibited times and distinguish between the permissibility of fard/wajib and nafl prayers.

Core Idea
Fard and wajib prayers are invalid at sunrise, zenith, and sunset; nafl is valid but disliked.

This passage from al-Jawhara al-Nayyirah explains the ruling on prayer during the three times when the sun is at specific positions: rising, at zenith, and setting. The commentator clarifies that the prohibition applies strictly to obligatory prayers (fard and wajib), while supererogatory prayers (nafl) are permissible but disliked. He also discusses the linguistic nuance of the matn's wording and provides an exception for the Asr prayer of the same day.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
The text explicitly states that prayer is not permissible at sunrise, at the sun's zenith (midday), and at sunset. Note that these are three distinct times, each with its own duration (sunrise and sunset last about the length of a spear or two).
The zenith prohibition is for when the sun is at its highest point, just before noon.
2
Determine which types of prayer are prohibited
The commentator specifies that the prohibition applies to make-up (qada) of obligatory prayers (fara'id) and wajibat, such as the prostration of recitation (sajda al-tilawa) and witr. Supererogatory prayers (nafl) are excluded from the absolute prohibition; they are valid but disliked.
The word 'salah' in the matn is interpreted as referring to the well-known obligatory prayers (al-ma'hood), not all prayers.
3
Understand the reason for the prohibition
The commentator explains that obligatory prayers were required in a complete form, so they cannot be performed during times that are considered incomplete (due to the sun's position). However, the Asr prayer of the same day is an exception because it was required in an incomplete form (its cause, the time, is incomplete).
This reasoning is based on the principle that an act required as complete cannot be fulfilled by an incomplete performance.
4
Recognize the exception for Asr
The text notes that performing Asr prayer on the same day (i.e., at its proper time even if it coincides with one of these times) is permissible because the prayer itself was prescribed as incomplete due to its cause being incomplete. This is a specific ruling unique to Asr.
This exception applies only to the current day's Asr, not to make-up of missed prayers.
5
Analyze the linguistic interpretation of 'al-salah'
The commentator addresses a potential confusion: the definite article in 'al-salah' (الصلاة) could imply generality, but it actually refers to the specific well-known obligatory prayer. This is a key usul point: the 'alif lam' for 'ahd (the well-known) restricts the ruling.
This linguistic analysis ensures that nafl is not included in the absolute prohibition.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books

وحجة صاحب «الهداية»: أنه لما ذكر الأوقات التي تُستحب فيها الصلاة: عقبه بذكر ما يقابله من الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة؛ ليتمكن المصلي من صلاته بغير كراهة تقع في صلاته من جانب الوقت. - وإنما لقب الباب بالكراهة، ثم بدأ بعدم الجواز؛ لأنه اعتبر الأغلب، والمكروه أكثر من عدم الجواز.
أو لأن الكراهة أعم من عدم الجواز ؛ لأن كل ما لا يجوز: فالكراهة فيه حاصلة أيضاً، كما هي ثابتة في المكروه، ولا يلزم من كل مكروه: أنه لا يجوز، فالكراهة ثابتةٌ في الصورتين، وليس عدم الجواز ثابتاً في الكراهة.
وهذه التسمية : مثل تسمية البيع الفاسد وإن انخرط فيه البيع الباطل.
لا تجوز الصلاة عند طلوع الشمس، ولا عند قيامها في الظهيرة، ولا عند غروبها .
قال رحمه الله: (لا تجوز الصلاة عند طلوع الشمس، ولا عند قيامها في الظهيرة، ولا عند غروبها).
يعني قضاء الفرائض، والواجبات الفائتة عن وقتها، كسجدة التلاوة التي وجبت بالتلاوة في وقت غير وقت مكروه، والوتر.
وإنما لا يجوز أداء الفرائض فيها؛ لأنها وجبت كاملة، فلا تتأدى بالناقص، حتى إنه يجوز عصر يومه ؛ لأنه وجب ناقصاً؛ لنقصان سببه.
فقوله : لا تجوز الصلاة عند طلوع الشمس: أراد ما سوى النفل
وفي «المشكل»: قوله : لا تجوز الصلاة ذَكَرَه معرفاً بالألف واللام، وهما لاستغراق الجنس، فينبغي أن لا يجوز التطوع، وليس كذلك، فإنه يجوز مع الكراهة، إلا أن وجهه أن الألف واللام هنا للمعهود، وهو الفرض، فينصرف عدم الجواز إليه فقط.
فنقول : إن كان المراد بقوله : لا تجوز الصلاة النفل : فمعناه: لا يجوز فعلها شرعاً، أما لو شرع فيها وفَعَلَها جاز، وإن شرع فيها وقطعها: يجب عليه قضاؤها.
وإن كان المراد : الفرض: لا يجوز أصلاً.
قوله : عند طلوع الشمس : حد الطلوع : قَدْرُ رمح أو رمحين.
Chapter on the times when prayer is disliked.
It would have been better to mention this chapter in the chapter on prayer times, as in al-Hidayah. But the author mentioned it here because dislike is among the incidental rulings, resembling missing the prayer, so the two chapters are homogeneous.
The proof of the author of al-Hidayah: when he mentioned the times when prayer is recommended, he followed it by mentioning the opposite: the times when prayer is disliked, so that the worshipper can perform his prayer without dislike occurring in his prayer from the side of the time. He titled the chapter with dislike, then started with non-permissibility, because he considered the majority, and the disliked is more than non-permissible. Or because dislike is more general than non-permissibility; for everything that is not permissible, dislike is also present in it, as it is established in the disliked, but not every disliked thing is necessarily impermissible. So dislike is established in both cases, while non-permissibility is not established in the disliked.
This naming is like naming a sale 'fasid' even though it includes the null sale.
Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor at its zenith in midday, nor at sunset.
He (may Allah have mercy on him) said: (Prayer is not permissible at sunrise, nor at its zenith in midday, nor at sunset).
He means the make-up of obligatory prayers and obligatory deeds missed from their time, such as the prostration of recitation that became obligatory due to recitation at a non-disliked time, and witr.
The performance of obligatory prayers during these times is not permissible because they were required as complete, so they cannot be fulfilled by an incomplete act. Indeed, it is permissible for the afternoon prayer on its day because it was required as incomplete due to the incompleteness of its cause.
So his statement: 'Prayer is not permissible at sunrise' means other than supererogatory.
In al-Mushkil: His statement: 'Prayer is not permissible' – he mentioned it with the definite article 'alif lam', and these indicate generality of the genus, so it would imply that supererogatory is also not permissible, but it is not so, for it is permissible with dislike. However, the explanation is that the 'alif lam' here refers to the well-known (al-ma'hood), which is the obligatory, so the non-permissibility applies only to it.
We say: If by his statement 'Prayer is not permissible' he meant supererogatory, then its meaning is: it is not permissible to perform it legally. But if one begins it and performs it, it is valid, and if he begins it and cuts it off, he must make it up. And if he meant obligatory, it is absolutely not permissible.
His statement: 'At sunrise' – the limit of sunrise is the length of a spear or two spears.
Source pages p. 427

Commentary
This passage is a commentary on a ruling from al-Quduri regarding the times when prayer is prohibited. The commentator first justifies the placement of this chapter after the chapter on recommended times, explaining that the author of al-Hidayah placed it there to contrast the disliked times with the recommended ones. He then discusses the terminology: the chapter title uses 'disliked' (karahah) but the body starts with 'non-permissible' (adam al-jawaz). The commentator clarifies that karahah is more general; everything not permissible is also disliked, but not all disliked things are impermissible. Then the core ruling is stated: prayer is not permissible at sunrise, midday zenith, and sunset. The commentator specifies that this refers to make-up (qada) of obligatory (fard) prayers and wajibat like sajdah al-tilawah and witr. The reason is that these acts were required in a complete form, so they cannot be performed during these incomplete times. However, the afternoon prayer of the same day is an exception because its cause (the time) is incomplete. The commentator further analyzes the phrasing: the definite article 'al-salah' might be interpreted as general, but it is actually specific to the well-known obligatory prayer, not supererogatory. Supererogatory prayer during these times is permissible but disliked. Finally, the time limit for sunrise is defined as the length of one or two spears, based on hadith.

Key Terms
لا تجوز (la tajuz): Meaning 'is not permissible', indicating prohibition (tahrim) for fard prayers.
الفرائض (al-fara'id): Obligatory prayers (fard 'ayn) and their make-up.
النفل (al-nafl): Supererogatory prayers, which are not obligatory.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the Hanafi school, what is the ruling on performing the make-up (qada) of Fajr prayer at sunrise?
A) It is permissible but disliked.
B) It is not permissible and invalid.
C) It is permissible without dislike.
D) It is permissible only if one begins it while the sun is still below the horizon.

Key Takeaway
Obligatory prayers (fard and wajib) are invalid at sunrise, zenith, and sunset; supererogatory prayers are valid but disliked; the exception is the current day's Asr which may be performed at sunset.

The Three Prohibited Times for Prayer
States the three times when prayer is invalid and clarifies which prayers are affected.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the three prohibited times for prayer and distinguish between the rulings for obligatory and supererogatory prayers at these times.

Core Idea
Missed obligatory prayers are invalid at sunrise, zenith, and sunset; supererogatory prayers are valid but disliked.

The Hanafi school identifies three times when prayer is restricted. However, the restriction applies differently to obligatory and voluntary prayers. This lesson clarifies which prayers are invalid and which are simply disliked, based on the matn of Al-Quduri and its commentary.

Guided Path
1
Identify the three prohibited times
List the three times mentioned: sunrise (when the sun is one or two spears above the horizon), zenith (noon when the sun is at its highest), and sunset.
The exact measurement of sunrise uses the spear-length standard.
2
Distinguish between fard/wajib and nafl
For missed obligatory prayers (qada), performing them at these times is absolutely invalid (batil). For supererogatory prayers, they are valid but makruh tahrimi (disliked close to prohibited).
The text uses 'la tajuzu aslan' for fard, indicating total invalidity.
3
Understand the exception for 'asr prayer
The 'asr prayer of the same day is permitted even during prohibited times because it became obligatory deficiently (due to a deficient cause), unlike other missed prayers which became obligatory in a complete state.
This highlights that the ruling depends on the nature of the obligation.
4
Define the limit of sunrise
Sunrise is defined as from when the sun appears until it rises to the height of one or two spears, i.e., until one can no longer look at its disk due to brightness.
This is a Hanafi-specific definition; other schools may differ.
5
Apply the ruling to practical scenarios
Given a specific time (e.g., 15 minutes after sunrise), determine whether a missed Fajr prayer is valid. Also, test a supererogatory prayer at the same time.
The outcome: Fajr qada is invalid; supererogatory is valid but disliked.

Source Text

وإنما لا يجوز أداء الفرائض فيها؛ لأنها وجبت كاملة، فلا تتأدى بالناقص، حتى إنه يجوز عصر يومه ؛ لأنه وجب ناقصاً؛ لنقصان سببه.

وفي المُصفّى»: ما دام يقدر على النظر إلى قرص الشمس: فهي في الطلوع: لا تباح الصلاة، فإذا عجز عن النظر: تباح.
Chapter of times when prayer is disliked. Prayer is not permitted at sunrise, nor at its zenith at noon, nor at sunset. He (the author) said: 'Prayer is not permitted at sunrise, nor at its zenith at noon, nor at sunset.' Meaning the making up of missed obligatory prayers and necessary prayers that have passed their time, like the prostration of recitation that became obligatory due to recitation at a time that is not disliked, and the witr prayer. And indeed, performing obligatory prayers in these times is not permitted because they became obligatory complete, so they cannot be performed deficiently, to the extent that the 'asr prayer of the same day is permitted because it became obligatory deficiently due to the deficiency of its cause. So his statement 'Prayer is not permitted at sunrise' intended other than supererogatory prayers. And in Al-Mushkil: his statement 'Prayer is not permitted' he mentioned it as definite with 'alif' and 'lam', and they are for encompassing the genus, so it would require that supererogatory prayer is not permitted, but it is not so, for it is permitted with dislike, except that the explanation is that 'alif' and 'lam' here are for the known, which is the obligatory prayer, so the non-permissibility is directed only to it. So we say: if what is meant by his statement 'Prayer is not permitted' is supererogatory prayer, then its meaning is: it is not legally permissible to perform it, but if one begins it and performs it, it is valid, and if one begins it and breaks it, he must make it up. And if what is meant is obligatory prayer: it is absolutely not permitted. His statement 'at sunrise': the limit of sunrise is the measure of one or two spears. And in Al-Musaffa: As long as one is able to look at the disk of the sun, it is in the state of sunrise: prayer is not permissible. When one is unable to look, it becomes permissible.
Source pages p. 428

Commentary
This passage is a ruling statement from the matn of Al-Quduri, expanded by the commentator. It identifies three times when prayer is not permitted: at sunrise, at the sun's zenith (noon), and at sunset. The commentator clarifies that this prohibition applies specifically to making up missed obligatory prayers (faraid) and necessary prayers (wajibat) like the prostration of recitation that became obligatory at a permissible time but was delayed, and the witr prayer. The reason is that these prayers became obligatory in a state of completeness, so they cannot be performed deficiently. In contrast, the 'asr prayer of the same day is permitted because its obligation was deficient from the start. The commentator then discusses the linguistic interpretation of 'la tajuzu' (not permitted). According to Al-Mushkil, the phrasing could be understood as absolute prohibition, but the context shows it refers only to obligatory prayers. For supererogatory prayers, they are valid with dislike (karahah). The definition of sunrise is given as when the sun is the height of one or two spears (approx. 3.5-7 meters above the horizon), until one can no longer look at the sun's disk due to its intensity. This is a Hanafi ruling; other schools may differ on the exact times and categories of prayer affected.

Key Terms
الطلوع (al-ṭulū‘): Sunrise; defined as when the sun is one or two spears above the horizon, until one cannot look at the disk.
الظهيرة (al-ẓahīra): The sun's zenith at noon; the time when the sun is at its highest point and shadows are shortest.
الرمح (al-rumḥ): A spear; used as a unit of measurement for the sun's height above the horizon.

Key Terms from Source Passage

A) It is valid but makruh.
B) It is invalid (batil).
C) It is valid without any dislike.
D) It is recommended.

Key Takeaway
Missed obligatory prayers are invalid at the three prohibited times; supererogatory prayers are valid but disliked.

Funeral Prayer and Sajdat al-Tilawah in Prohibited Times: Timing Matters
Ruling on two acts during prohibited times with condition on timing of obligation.

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on performing funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah during prohibited times and distinguish between cases where the obligation arose in a permissible time vs. the prohibited time.

Core Idea
If obligation arises in prohibited time, perform; if delayed from permissible time, invalid.

The Hanafi school recognizes that certain acts of worship, like funeral prayer and prostration of recitation, can be performed during the three prohibited times (sunrise, zenith, sunset) under specific conditions. The key distinction is whether the obligation first arose in a permissible time and was then delayed, or whether it arose directly within the prohibited time itself. This lesson unpacks that distinction and its practical implications.

Guided Path
1
Identify the two acts and the general rule
The passage discusses two acts: salat al-janazah (funeral prayer) and sajdat al-tilawah (prostration of recitation). The general rule is that performing these during prohibited times is not allowed under normal circumstances, with an exception tied to when the obligation arose.
The three prohibited times are: sunrise, zenith (when the sun is at its meridian), and sunset.
2
Understand the condition: when the obligation arose
The prohibition applies only if the act was already obligatory in a permissible time and was then delayed until a prohibited time. If the obligation itself arose during the prohibited time (e.g., death at sunrise or reciting a prostration verse at that moment), performing it in that time is valid.
The text uses the phrase 'أُخرتا إلى هذا الوقت' to indicate delay from a permissible time.
3
Apply the principle to funeral prayer
For funeral prayer, if death occurs during a prohibited time, the prayer can be performed immediately. The hadith 'Hasten with your dead' and the list of three matters not to be delayed support making performance preferable (afdal).
The obligation arises with the presence of the janazah; it is not tied to a specific clock time.
4
Apply the principle to sajdat al-tilawah
For sajdat al-tilawah, even if the obligation arose in a prohibited time, it is better to delay because the obligation is 'ala al-tarākhī (at leisure). It can be performed later in a permissible time without sin.
This contrasts with the funeral prayer, which demands immediacy.
5
Note the preference (afdaliyyah) and the proofs
The author explicitly answers the question of preference: for funeral prayer, performance in the prohibited time is better; for sajdat al-tilawah, delay is better. The proofs are the hadith for funeral and the concept of tarakhi for sajdat al-tilawah.
Distinguish between 'ja'iz' (permissible) and 'afdal' (better). Here both are permissible, but the best action differs.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
ولا يُصلي على جنازة، ولا يسجد للتلاوة،
وفي المُصفّى»: ما دام يقدر على النظر إلى قرص الشمس: فهي في الطلوع: لا تباح الصلاة، فإذا عجز عن النظر: تباح.
* قوله : (ولا يصلي على جنازة، ولا يسجد للتلاوة).
هذا إذا وجبتا في وقت مباح ، وأُخرتا إلى هذا الوقت : فإنه لا يجوز قطعاً. أما لو وجبتا في هذا الوقت، وأُديتا فيه جاز؛ لأنها أُديت ناقصة كما وجبت، إذ الوجوب : بحضور الجنازة، والتلاوة
فإن قلت: ما الأفضل الأداء، أو التأخير إلى وقت مباح؟
قلتُ: أما في صلاة الجنازة فالأفضل الأداء؛ لقوله عليه الصلاة والسلام: «عجلوا بموتاكم (۱).
وقال: اثلاث لا يُؤخَرْن : جنازةٌ ،أنت ودَيْن وجدت ما تقضيه، وبكر وجد لها كف (٢)
وأما في سجدة التلاوة فالأفضل التأخير ؛ لأن وجوبها على التراخي.
And he should not pray over a funeral, nor prostrate for recitation. And in Al-Musaffa: As long as he is able to look at the disk of the sun, it is in the state of sunrise: prayer is not permissible. When he is unable to look, it becomes permissible. * His statement: (He should not pray over a funeral, nor prostrate for recitation). This is when they become obligatory in a permissible time, and they are delayed to this time: then it is absolutely not permitted. However, if they become obligatory in this time, and are performed in it, it is permitted; because they are performed deficient as they became obligatory, since the obligation arises from the presence of the funeral and the recitation. If you ask: what is better, performance or delay to a permissible time? I say: as for funeral prayer, performance is better, due to his statement, peace be upon him: 'Hasten with your dead.' And he said: Three things should not be delayed: a funeral when it is present, a debt when you have something to repay it, and a virgin when she has a match. As for the prostration of recitation, delay is better because its obligation is at leisure.
Source pages p. 429

Commentary
This passage addresses the ruling on funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) and prostration of recitation (sajdat al-tilawah) during the three prohibited times. The commentator explains that if these acts become obligatory during a permissible time (e.g., the funeral is present before sunrise) but are intentionally delayed until a prohibited time, then performing them during the prohibited time is invalid (la yajuzu qat'an). However, if the obligation arises directly during the prohibited time (e.g., someone dies at sunrise, or a verse of prostration is recited at that time), then performing them is permissible because the act is performed in the same state of deficiency in which it became obligatory. For funeral prayer, the preference is to perform it immediately even during a prohibited time, based on the hadith 'Hasten with your dead' and the principle that three matters should not be delayed. For sajdat al-tilawah, it is better to delay until a permissible time because its obligation is not immediate (ala al-tarakhi).

Key Terms
جنازة (janāzah): Funeral; specifically the funeral prayer (salat al-janazah) which is a collective obligation.
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilāwah): Prostration of recitation; an act of worship performed when reciting or hearing specific verses of the Quran.
التراخي (al-tarākhī): Leisure; the obligation of sajdat al-tilawah is not immediate but can be delayed to a permissible time.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint

A) It is invalid and must be delayed.
B) It is valid and preferable to perform immediately.
C) It is valid but makruh to perform immediately.
D) It is not allowed at all.

Key Takeaway
For funeral prayer, perform immediately even in prohibited time if death occurs then; for sajdat al-tilawah, delay to permissible time because its obligation is at leisure.

Prayer During Disliked Times and the Exception for Asr
States prohibition and exception for Asr, includes sujood al-tilawah ruling

Learning Objective
By the end of this lesson, you will be able to state the Hanafi ruling on prayer during disliked times, identify the exception for Asr, and explain the legal reasoning for the prohibition of sujood al-tilawah during those times.

Core Idea
Prayer during disliked times is makruh, not invalid; only Asr at sunset is valid because it was obligated deficiently.

This passage from the Hidayah clarifies the intent of the chapter on disliked times. It addresses a key ambiguity: while the primary text says 'prayer is disliked', it specifies that funeral prayer and sujood al-tilawah are merely disliked, not invalid. Master this distinction to understand when an act is valid but blameworthy versus when it becomes invalid.

Guided Path
1
Identify the act and its ruling
The passage discusses prayer during disliked times. Identify that the base ruling for funeral prayer and sajdat al-tilawah is karahah (dislike), meaning the acts are valid but blameworthy.
The text explicitly says 'al-karahah', not 'al-haram'.
2
Locate the exception
Note the exception for Asr prayer of the same day at sunset. Understand that this exception is due to the deficient nature of the obligation at that time.
Asr at sunset is performed as it was obligated – deficiently.
3
Trace the dalil for the qahqaha analogy
The text includes a question about why loud laughter does not attach to prostration alone. Analyze the hadith and the interpretation of 'al-Salah' as meaning the complete prayer with tahrimah.
The definite article in 'al-Salah' indicates a specific complete prayer.
4
Distinguish between sunrise and sunset
Compare the invalidation of Fajr prayer at sunrise with the validity of Asr prayer at sunset. The key difference is exiting to a disliked time vs. entering a new prayer time.
Sunrise exits Fajr time to a non-prayer time; sunset enters Maghrib time.
5
Evaluate the practical implications
Understand how this ruling applies: one should avoid praying at disliked times but does not need to repeat if done; only Fajr at sunrise is invalid.
Knowing this prevents unnecessary repetition of prayers.

Source Text
⚠ Extracted via Advanced OCR ∼97% accuracy, minor errors may remain — always verify against original Arabic books
باب الأوقات التي تكره فيها الصلاة
إلا عصر يومه عند غروب الشمس .
وفي «الهداية»(۱) : المراد بالنهي المذكور في صلاة الجنازة، وسجدة التلاوة: الكراهة، حتى لو صلاها فيه، أو تلا سجدة فيه، وسجدها: جاز؛ لأنها أديت ناقصةً كما وجبت.
قوله : ولا يسجد للتلاوة: لأنها في معنى الصلاة.
فإن قلت: لم ألحقت هنا بالصلاة ولم تلحق بها في القهقهة، مع أن النبي صلى الله عليه وسلم قال: «مَن ضحك منكم قهقهة: فليعد الوضوء، والصلاة (٢).
قلت: عدم الإلحاق هناك باعتبار أن الألف واللام في قوله: فليعد الصلاة للعهد، وإنما الصلاة المعهودة هي ذات التحريمة والركوع والسجود، فلا تتناول السجود مجرداً من غير تحريمة.
وأما هنا النهي عن الصلاة في هذه الأوقات؛ كي لا يقع التشبه بمَن يعبد الشمس، وبالسجود : يحصل التشبه أيضاً : فكره.
قوله : (إلا عصر يومه عند غروب الشمس؛ لأن السبب هو الجزء القائم من الوقت، وذلك الجزء القائم من الوقت ناقص؛ لأنه آخر وقت العصر، فقد أداها كما وجبت.
بخلاف غيرها من الصلوات؛ لأنها وجبت كاملةً، فلا تتأدى بالناقص.
ولو طلعت عليه الشمس وهو في صلاة الفجر: فسدت صلاته.
بخلاف ما إذا غربت على مصلي العصر، حيث لا تفسد.
والفرق: أنها إذا غربت: فقد دخل وقت المغرب، فيكون مؤدياً في وقت، وأما إذا طلعت فقد خرج لا إلى وقت بل هو وقت مكروه، ففسدت.
Chapter on times when prayer is disliked, except the Asr of that day at sunset. And in Al-Hidayah: The intended meaning of the prohibition mentioned regarding funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is dislike (karahah), such that if one prays them in that time or recites a prostration and prostrates, it is permissible; because it was performed deficiently as it was obligated. He said: Do not prostrate for recitation because it is in the meaning of prayer. If you say: Why is it attached to prayer here but not attached to it in loud laughter, while the Prophet said: Whoever among you laughs loudly, let him repeat both the ablution and the prayer. I say: The lack of attachment there is because the definite article in his saying 'the prayer' (al-Salah) is for a specific pact, and the specific prayer is the one with the opening takbir (tahrimah), bowing, and prostration, so it does not include prostration alone without a takbir. As for here, the prohibition of prayer in these times is to avoid resemblance to those who worship the sun, and by prostration, resemblance also occurs, so it is disliked. He said: Except the Asr of that day at sunset; because the cause is the part of the time that remains, and that part is deficient since it is the end of the Asr time, so he performs it as it was obligated. Unlike other prayers, because they were obligated complete, so they are not performed deficiently. And if the sun rises while he is in the Fajr prayer, his prayer is invalidated. Unlike if the sun sets on the one praying Asr, where it is not invalidated. The difference: when it sets, the Maghrib time has entered, so he is performing in a time; but when it rises, it has exited not to a time but to a disliked time, so it is invalidated.
Source pages p. 430

Commentary
This passage is a ruling with proof from the Hidayah explaining the chapter on times when prayer is disliked. The author first clarifies that the prohibition mentioned for funeral prayer and prostration of recitation is one of dislike (karahah), not absolute prohibition. If one performs these acts during disliked times, they are valid but deficient, since they were obligated deficiently (like Asr at its end). He then discusses why the ruling of not prostrating for tilawah applies: prostration is like prayer in meaning. A questioner raises an objection: why is loud laughter attached to prayer here but not in the case of qahqaha (laughter during prayer requiring repetition of wudu and salah)? The answer is that the hadith 'let him repeat the prayer' refers to the complete prayer with takbir, bowing, and prostration, not a mere prostration. Here, the similarity to sun-worshippers is the reason for dislike. Next, the exception for Asr of the same day at sunset is explained: the cause is the remaining portion of the time, which is deficient; the prayer is performed as it was obligated (deficiently). Other prayers are obligated complete, so they cannot be performed deficiently. A distinction is made between sunrise during Fajr (invalidates) and sunset during Asr (does not invalidate): when the sun sets, Maghrib time begins, so he is still in a valid time; when the sun rises, the time exits to a disliked time, thus invalidating the prayer.

Key Terms
سجدة التلاوة (sajdat al-tilawah): Prostration of recitation performed when reciting specific Quranic verses.
الكراهة (al-karahah): Legal dislike; an action that is not prohibited but is better to avoid.
القهقهة (al-qahqaha): Loud, audible laughter that disrupts prayer.
التحريمة (al-tahrimah): The opening takbir (Allahu Akbar) that begins the prayer, which renders worldly actions forbidden during prayer.

Key Terms from Source Passage

Checkpoint
According to the passage, why is the Asr prayer of the same day excepted from the prohibition of prayer at disliked times?
A) Because it is a wajib prayer.
B) Because it was obligated deficiently (naqisan) and is performed as such.
C) Because it can be performed at any time.
D) Because it is a sunnah prayer.

Key Takeaway
Prayer during disliked times is generally valid but disliked (makruh tanzih), with the exception of Asr at sunset because it was obligated deficiently, and the invalidation of Fajr prayer at sunrise.
